RATING: 9
The game doesn't get to the table very often because the sessions are long, but we just love being immersed in the Verse. Maybe you have to be a Firefly fan to love it - I don't know - but we are and we do. However, I don't think just putting a theme or license you love on a game by default makes it a good game. I love "The Princess Bride" but I haven't found a game with that theme that I felt was very good. "Firefly: The Game" not only lets us live in that universe again, one that was taken from us way too soon, but the game play is fun. I need to hire a crew and get supplies so I can travel to places to get missions and complete missions and avoid Reavers. We love it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Virtually everyone else has already said it, but it's still true: If you love the show, you'll love the game. I love the show, so I have a hard time saying how I'd feel about the game if I didn't.

The common criticism that I've heard is that there's low player interaction. I mostly agree; the interaction is indirect and/or friendly such as it is in Catan (I can send a hostile unit against you, I can take something you want before you get to it, even if it's primarily to benefit myself, and I can trade with you so that we both get what we need).

What I dislike about the game the most is that so many crew, ships and gear are generic. You can hire as many gun hands, enforcers and scrappers as you want, and equip them with pistols, explosive charges and improvised hacking rigs. I'd have preferred each gun hand to have his own name and to have a make and model for the guns, even if they were just made up by GF9. They also left out several major guest characters.

As far as gameplay goes, a method of attacking other crews in the official rules would have been nice, but I have a feeling that may be coming in an expansion.

Even with the generic crew and gear, there is still plenty of unique crew, captains and gear, as well as a variety of different story cards that will lead to extensive replay.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

The gameplay itself is too simplistic, and the events that occur make for a somewhat incoherent collage of things copied directly from the show and seen exclusively through the eyes of its characters.

RATING: 8.5
Uno de los mejores ameritrash que he probado, de los más temáticos donde sientes como estás jugando identificándote con las aventuras de la serie, en la posición de capitán de una nave Firefly.
Dos acciones por jugador en el turno, que no se pueden repetir: volar, comprar tripulantes/equipo, conseguir nuevas misiones, realizar trabajos. 
Elección de objetivos finales de la partida, decenas de cartas de tripulantes, equipamiento nave/tripulantes, mejoras de la nave, etc.
Tensión por el crucero de la alianza y por la nave de los reavers.
En definitiva mucha variedad e inmersión en un juego cargado de mucho azar (cartas cuando vuelas, dado) que implica en este caso tensión, emoción y diversión.
No esperéis grandes mecánicas, es básicamente un pick-up & deliver como mecánica principal, tipo el Merchant of Venus, pero mucho mas abierto y con más libertad, y con pruebas continuas de cartas para tirar un dado donde se suma la habilidad de la tripulación y su equipación que hubierais adquirido. 
A mi gusto le falta eso sí más elementos de interacción, como el que tiene de comprar a los jugadores descontentos de otro jugador si compartes mismo espacio.

PD: Imprescindible ver la serie y luego la película Serenity para involucrarse más.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Another one of those amazing games I rarely get on the table due to it's complexity and time requirement.

I'm a Browncoat, so I immediately took to this game. The theming is obviously done with great love and attention, and it shows. This isn't a reskin of a boring game with TV characters plastered on. This game is a ground-up creation, factoring in many critical moments, characters, and issues from the show. If you're a Firefly fan, you should check this out.

Pros:
- Theme: As I said, WONDERFUL theming. Characters "act" as they would in the show. Locations and items feel like artifacts from Firefly. The creators obviously had a passion for authenticity and it shows.
- Mechanics: This game is essentially Diet Light D&D In Space. You perform skill rolls frequently that items, characters, and abilities can adjust. You get into conflicts with several ways out. This isn't a Munchkin-style "Kill anything you meet" game. You can use diplomacy, cleverness, or weaponry to get out of a jam.
- Bits: The parts in this game are wonderfully constructed. Ships are hefty plastic chunks and feel sturdy. The money (HOLY COW THE MONEY) feels and smells and looks AMAZING. The dice are great, and the board, cards, and box all have stellar art and graphic design. Imagine Bioshock's art mixed with a Western flair, and you're halfway there.

Cons:
- Length: This game takes time. HOURS. A 2 person game took us at least 2-3 hours. It's a "whole evening" game, not a fun -1hr game.
- Chance: This game has just a BIT too much reliance on chance and luck. Dice rolls and card pulls can be devastating, even if you've played well so far. I wish it was a bit more informed by player agency.
- Rules: It's not as complicated as other hefty games (Android, Twilight Imperium, etc), but it's still a doozy. Be prepared to spend a good amount of time in "tutorial mode" for new players.
- Boring? A bit. A large amount of the game will be spent carting people and cargo to and fro. The event cards, random encounters, and moving Alliance and Reaper vessels keep it tense, but still, at it's heart, it's a pick-up-and-carry game. After 4 hrs of play, it starts to show through.

I recommend this for any fans of the show, and anyone who gets tingles at the thought of owning a ship, modding it with equipment, enlisting and upgrading a crew of individuals who have unique strengths and weaknesses, and trying to hack it in the bleak dangerous black of space.

RATING: 8
DRIPPING WITH THEME. The rules are organized horribly, but the rulebook itself is a joy to read, with all the Firefly quotes and fun vernacular/colloquialisms. The minis are nicely modeled, will paint.
Gameplay is pretty simple, but there is good variety in the Jobs, Nav, and Supply cards. Gameplay theme is spot on, which carries the somewhat less-than-innovative game mechanics.
Oh, and the paper money in this is the -only- good paper money I've found in a game. It is beautiful, quite thick, and (once again) SUPER-THEMEY.

RATING: 9
Merchants of Venus + Firefly universe = OH MY G-D THE THEME MAKES THIS AWESOME!

If you like Firefly, YOU MUST PLAY THIS!!!  If you don't like Firefly, you are dead to me.  (Just sayin'.)

Objectively, the game is very luck-driven -- card draws, dice rolls, luck is everywhere you look.  Your choices do influence your ability to respond to this luck so it's not entirely unmitigated.  And you have goals to accomplish with choices (sometimes) as to how you accomplish them (or at least how you get from point A to point B and how fast you get from A to B).  But objectively the game isn't fantastic or amazing or anything.  It's Merchants of Venus with some stuff.

BUT THE THEME!  OH THE THEME!  AND LO I SHALL CONTINUE TYPING IN CAPITAL LETTERS BECAUSE THE THEME IS THAT AWESOME.  IT IS!  IT'S IMPLEMENTED VERY WELL SUCH THAT THE GAME GIVES THE FEELING LIKE YOU'RE A CAPTAIN (MAL!) PILOTING YOUR SHIP IN THE FIREFLY UNIVERSE.  ("WOOT!  I FIND RIVER AND HIRE HER FOR MY SHIP!  MWUAHAHAHA!!!"  Oh Summer Glau, wherefor art thou?  *cough*  *cough*)

I WILL PROBABLY OWN THIS GAME.  BECAUSE I KEEP TYPING IN CAPITAL LETTERS.  BECAUSE I MUST.  BECAUSE I'D BE A BROWNCOAT IF I WENT IN FOR THAT COSPLAY OR RPG THING.

That holds it back a bit for me, but I like what it's doing overall.

RATING: 10
As an avid devotee of Firefly, I was somewhat dubious when it came out in a board game. Often, these things are such a disappointment.
My initial foray into the game was with 5 players, and not enough time. The second game didn't fare much better either.
However, I persevered, acquired the game myself, and after some practice, realised that the only thing wrong with the game is the Playing Time printed on the side of the box.
It is not a short game to play.
It is however, an excellent game for Firefly fans.
The 'colour' in the game, and the game mechanics are very much in the style of the series.
Advice: do as they say and keep your eye on the Supply and Contact decks. I does speed things up.
THIS IS A GOOD GAME.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I wasn't a fan of the tv series; its Wild West in space theming seemed both implausible and lazy (space, the wild frontier - geddit? Yes).  I'll have to take the word of other commenters that Firefly is true to its theme.  There is certainly a shed load of characters and stuff, and while it is possible to operate as a law abiding trader, there are abundant temptations to take up the outlaw life.

Firefly is frequently likened to Merchant of Venus and indeed both are games in which picking up and delivering is repeated for rather too long.  That and the game play is solitaire-ish; the other players are just downtime between your turns.  There is also a hatful of random elements from card draws for just about everything to dice rolls to overcome challenges.  The luck can be mitigated, but still it can screw you. A jolly wild frontier narrative gives Firefly some appeal, but ultimately it isn't quite enough.

Production quality is excellent, though the artwork is uninspired.

However, I spoke with the designer and told me of an upcoming expansion will allow a much more, "take that" and aggressive interaction play style.  I am looking forward to this but enjoy the game as is as well.  GF9 has done with this license translation.

RATING: 8
Questing In Space!

This game is cool, but it takes up a LOT of space (no pun intended). You'll need a big table for this one.

It's like Twilight Imperium Lite! Sorta. You don't build an armada, you just have your one ship that you fly between planets and space stations. When you fly to some space stations or planets, you can interact with "contacts" or "shops," which each have a deck of cards you draw from to get missions or items.

The overall goal is to hire crew members and make money, with different win conditions based on the scenario you choose.

RATING: 7.5
Some words of advice...  if a game box tells you what to do in 3 simple statements.  Something like: Find a crew, Find a job, Keep flying... Then it makes a lot more sense to do what it says than trying to mix it up and do it in your own order.  Why?  Because if you ignore the straight up advice, your game is going to run a long, long time.  Far longer than even the series this game was based on was on the air.  Okay - so that aside.  

For fans of the series, this game is actually quite well done.  It really captures the feel and the look from the show.  The game play is solid, if a tad drawn out - which is not a problem for fans, but may not tickle the fancy of those with unenlightened souls.  Overall production is really great.  The box is filled with Firefly goodies.  Add in the expansions out in the 'verse and you have a game that will delight fans.  For non-fans, they are likely to find a good pick up and deliver game with a lot of chrome.  Sometimes chrome can make a game and this is one such title.  Just remember to do what the box says (and in the right order!)

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This is an interesting take on the Firefly license. It's not a game of thrilling heroics - it's a merchant ship simulator. You'll be doing very little wisecracking, and very much taking mail from the depot to the border planets.

The turn-to-turn gameplay is pretty fun and satisfying, and each individual piece is fine. The game is far too long for its experience, though - the 2-hour estimate is a joke, and you can expect to spend 4-5 hours on a game.

I'm considering, as a house rule, reducing the max crew to 4 but giving everyone +2 to all rolls. Get things rolling faster.

One other complaint is that the rules use Firefly quips as rules terms. It's fine once you get used to it, but makes learning the game that much harder. For example, 'Kosherized' (can't use icons on weapons). 'Aiming to Misbehave' (random challenge deck). 'Keep Flyin' (no random event)

So yeah, I won't be tearing my hair out if I end up playing this again, but I think it missed the mark on creating 'The Firefly Boardgame'.

RATING: 8
10/26/15
Decided to rate finally after it has been requested by my family and has been burning a hole in my conscious to get back to the table. As a fan of the series and of good writing and acting in general, I feel connected to the story that was created while playing the game. Not as the characters I know, despite the cards I may select as captain, but as a member of that verse and in that period. Its an uncanny feeling that adds a lot to the play time. For me that is the strength of this one, my siblings not all of which have ever watched an episode, got that from it, and in the end its about sitting down and enjoying the experience, this games mechanics work in this presentation and the sum is way more than the parts together and comes out to something special on my table.

Have not rated this one yet as there are only solo plays of it, I have had an absolute blast with what is here, but still solo. Group play is coming soon and I will have a better idea then. For now this one is a solidly put together and produced game that produces a nice bit of tension on every move. Replicating nicely the sense of wonder, awe, and dread that those characters who inhabited this verse on the fiction would have had. It also brings a bit more and here is where it shines: it conveys a sense of familiarity, accomplishment and yes confidence also, you have to act the part if you want to be the part. While a lot of this is board gaming in general, that particular trait serves this ip very well. I am a fan of a lot on offer here: the franchise, roll play, die rolling, paper money, even the actors on the cards, so yes there was a lot for me to like anyway. However the uninitiated with the show should still enjoy this romp of a thematic game if they enjoy the mechanics involved and the unique brand of flavor this setting delivers. A very deliberated upon rating will come soon, but suffice to say I like this one a lot.

RATING: 7
Firefly takes one part Merchant of Venus, one part Talisman, sprinkles in the cast and setting of Firefly...then bakes the whole thing at 350 degrees for 2 hours.  What comes out of the oven might be one of the most entertaining pick up and delivery style games ever made.  Calling it a Pick Up and delivery game is almost a disservice to the game in the box though.  It's more of a thrilling cosmic adventure game!  It's got so much going on, but it's very easy and smooth to play.  I love the mechanic of flipping cards over to move around...it creates this palpable sense of fear.  The nice part is it makes sense thematically from the show.  Also most cards give you a couple of options which is always cool too.  The game has dice, but they don't dominate the game.  Man, everything just feels right.  I happen to love the show and the game doesn't disappoint.  This is dream come true type of game...and Gale Force 9 delivered.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is one of the best board games I've played to date.  I went into it skeptical because I was worried that someone may have just picked up a popular license and threw together a half-assed game to make a few bucks off the fans.  That is most definitely not the case here.

Firefly captures the flavor of the TV series and movie pretty darn well.  For example the abilities (which each 'crew member' has variations of) possessed by River Tam are random each time you head into an 'event', but can be partially controlled if you also have her brother Simon Tam on your crew.  Still, even if it had nothing to do with Firefly the game play/mechanics could stand on their own.  (Just to note: Some people think the River/Simon combo is broken... I do not for a second. There are other crew I much prefer over them).

At first glance, and even during your first game, Firefly will likely intimidate even fairly hard core gamers.  It is a game that simply reading the rules is not going to do it for you... you must play this game 2-3 times before you really get a completely solid grasp on a personal strategy and it might take more if you don't really pay attention to everything you can do/get and where you can do/get it.  There are 13 decks of cards, half a dozen or more types of tokens, the ships, a good sized board, dice, and various other odds and ends used in this game.  The game has a LARGE footprint.  It will cover a 3.5ftx5ft table pretty well... and that's without the expanded board that "Blue Sun" adds on to it.  Your first game will be slow, it's going to take you 3-4 hours... but once you pick it up it starts moving along and 2 hours is a more reasonable estimate.

Last note, in my opinion you can choose to ignore the various scenarios the game comes with and simply set a time limit, adding up the valuables that all the various players have to determine the winner if you like.  This means if you want a quicker or longer game you are not tied to a specific goal the game has set for the players to win.

RATING: 8
Gale Force Nine really does an incredible job of handling IP's. If you love theme baked into every fiber of the play experience, you owe yourself to check into games like Firefly, Spartacus, and Sons of Anarchy. I disagree with some others in that I absolutely feel that this board game captures the essence of the show. The decision points in "keeping flying" is balanced with regard to keeping a good and happy crew. There slower momemts of developing simple plans at a comfortable pace and there are tense moments when you have to push a situation farther than you like. The other players are your competitors - but with a civility among rogues. Really, the game is charming as was the show. I like the show; though it doesn't blow me away like other IP's do, it's charming and consistently likeable. That's also so how I feel about the game. It's a wonderful way to spend a gaming afternoon with friends when the week has already provided enough stress such that you don't want to have too much on your weekend, too. It won't change your world, but if you're in the mood for a narrative building game, Firefly offers a beautifully deep world into which you can immerse yourself. Yes, randomness plays a larger role than might be comfortable for some (card draws are important). Someone who presses their luck can win big over someone who performs who makes the smart decisions and comes up dry. If this could bother you, the game either isn't for you or it's not for the mood you're in. I'm not always in the mood for Firefly myself. When I am, though, it's a pleasant, rich place to be. All expansions are recommended, most particularly Blue Sun, Kalidasa, and Breakin' Atmo.

RATING: 10
Essentially "Merchants and Marauders" in space. You have a ship which is used to get and complete "jobs" (often pick-up and deliver) for which you get paid. You can visit various "contacts" to get the jobs and other locations where additional crew can be hired, your ship upgraded, or you can select gear with which to outfit your crew. Jobs can involve the delivery of cargo (possibly contraband), passengers (possibly fugitives), or could be an illegal act such as robbing a bank or any number of questionable activities. In the course of this some members of your crew can become "disgruntled," you can be attacked by Reavers, or boarded by Alliance forces searching "outlaw ships" such as those carrying illegal cargo, fugitives or "wanted" crew members. The base game includes a number of scenarios with varying objectives not all necessarily involving being the Richest Captain in the 'Verse. Player interaction is at best indirect as there are no player vs player elements, but there are situations where your actions can interfere with or complicate other players' progress. One of the expansions fixes this if you must have it (Pirates & Bounty Hunters) but I found the game challenging enough without also having to contend with your opponent's attacks.

Thematically, it is very true to the short-lived Joss Whedon TV series of the same name (and the movie: "Serenity"). It is a "space western" in much the same manner as "Merchants and Marauders" is a swashbuckler. In fact they play very much alike. There is a fair amount of die rolling in both games but each case you can help your cause by the careful accumulation of crew, ship upgrades and gear which yield die-roll mods and/or key items without which your job could be botched, or worse.

I like to think of it as a "beer & pretzels" experience not meant to be taken too seriously. The bits are well done, colourful and very thematic. The artwork and flavour text are evocative and tongue-in-cheek similar to the style of the series being an odd mixture of Buck Rogers and Tom Mix. The cards, and there are many of them, beg to be read aloud as they are being considered or resolved rather than simply, "oh, here's a gun skill check - I need a seven." Another way of saying that those who might get the most fun out of this game would be fans of the old TV series. I really like Merchants and Marauders as the best of the pirate-themed games; but, given the choice and for a similar experience (but now set in space), I would play this.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Provisional rating, I might get bored with it ... but as a fan of the show this is about as good as it gets :)

Helps if you know the show/film and like it. But fans of pickup/deliver will find stuff here they'll enjoy too.

Downsides, maybe a bit too long for some and player interaction is a bit limited.

Overall, shiny :)

RATING: 9.2
The more I play this game and the more I re-watch Firefly, the more I love this game (and Firefly). 

I'm interested in the Blue Sun expansion, I don't think the base game will hold my attention forever. A dozen plays maybe, but not forever. 

Great game. Always been a hit with Firefly fans, the one person with whom I played who had not seen the show also enjoyed it.

A note about length. The complaint I've heard about this game is that it is too long. I disagree and here's why- whenever I teach to a new player, I say, "we're going to play for 1 hour and whoever had the most money at that time wins." Every time the hour comes and the person says, "Can we please keep playing?" I had to cut my little sister off after four hours on Thanksgiving. The game can be played very openly and that can lead to indefinite playing times- but that's because everyone is having fun literally "playing" in the Firefly universe. 

Great game, a no-brainer for any fan of the show.

RATING: 6
I loved this game so much–at first. Two hours in, I couldn't wait for it to end. 

The first part of the game is spent getting crew, installing cool upgrades, and fulfilling missions, traveling across the galaxy. Woohoo! The second half of the game was spent rolling dice. And rolling dice. And rolling and rolling and rolling. And often failing. Three turns I spent in a single spot. Half of my turns were lost by bad rolls or bad draws while flying.

"Lose a turn" is my least favorite mechanic in any game. That alone dropped my rating from an "8." We may try a variant to allow repeating failed actions (e.g. move-move if your first action was stopped by the Reavers/Alliance; work-work if your first action was a failed skill check, etc.); hopefully this might speed the game up and cut down on the number of lost turns.

UPDATE: We like this more with the pure money scenarios. The game moves faster and there aren't nearly as many dice checks. It still can be frustrating with bad draws/rolls/lost turns, but at least it feels thematic.

RATING: 4
The theme is very strong. I'm pretty sure this game would be unappealing to anyone unfamiliar with the show. Once you get past how deeply the theme goes, the game itself is fairly flawed. The difficulty of the "misbehave" cards seems to range from "piece of cake" to "only possible if you have a particular card," and since these come up randomly, this mechanic feels broken. Some have serious consequences for not meeting the objective, while others have no consequences at all. It seems like the winner is the person who gets screwed over by the game the least, but all the screwage is determined by random chance. If I wanted to be randomly screwed by a game, I'd play Candyland and get it over with much more quickly.

RATING: 7
*7* (3+ Plays)
This game is tough to evaluate. I want to like it more because it looks so cool. The game is definitely longer than advertised and lots of table space is going to be needed. There is a mix of luck and strategy in the game that takes experience to understand how to balance it. There are lots of cards to go through in game play, so knowing what to expect or look for will definitely help. The theme is great and I do enjoy the game because of the decisions to make. My favorite part is buying crew and equipment. Lots of cool combinations can be achieved with all the cards and scenario's. My biggest gripe with the game is the length of play, it's just too long, so it makes it very difficult to get to the table. I do think this game is great, when I get the opportunity to play it. It's a keeper for me and I hope to log many more plays.

RATING: 7.5
Sell

In this game you take on the role of a captain flying around the 'verse trying to complete the main mission objective before the other players. 

You need to upgrade your ship, hire crew, get weapons and money, all the while avoiding the authorities and the reavers. You become 'solid' with the shadowy figures of the 'verse to earn more cash and then use this to get the necessary skills/weapons/upgrades to complete the main mission. 

Highly thematic, and will be most appreciated by Firefly fans. The components are also excellent. The game plays up to four players, however I think it could be prone to some significant downtime with more players. 

Overall a very shiny game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A few plays in, impressions are good. It's fundamentally a pick up and deliver game, but the different types of missions from the different characters (Badger, Niska, etc), along with the different scenarios, make it interesting.

In some ways this game reminds me of [i]Merchant & Marauders[/i], except that the crew members are more specialized and you need to tailor your crew for the types of missions you plan to take. The morale/disgruntled aspect is a nice touch, too.

You can't attack other players, though you can mess with them indirectly using the Alliance or Reaver ships on occasion. That's one advantage [i]Merchants & Marauders[/i] has over this game, though in practice actual attacks on other players in M&M don't happen so much as the [i]threat[/i] of attacks on other players, so maybe it's not such a big deal.

The game has taken some heat for both playing time and luck. I think the playing time issue is solvable with experience and by simply capping the number of players at three. Four is a bit much. Also, a simple house rule allowing both moseying and regular jumps on the same turn could help. As for luck, well, there are plenty of things you can do to mitigate it. The people whining about it probably skimped on the equipment and/or crew members that could have helped them, and got burned as a result. And keep in mind that the worm usually turns for everyone at some point, so don't panic because of one bad die roll because your opponents will probably get some bad luck of their own at some point.

Criticism regarding the rulebook, however, is warranted. It's definitely a bit on the weak side, as born out by a rather large number of rules questions here and the lengthy FAQ. Be sure to get the FAQ and go over that. The lack of a player aid also annoys me, though there's a decent one in the files section.

Still, thumbs up overall.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9

You're a wheeler-dealer in a Firefly-class freighter who hires a crew then accomplishes a series of missions given you by a collection of shady characters, all while avoiding the Alliance patrols (the cops) and the crazy Reavers. RATING: 6
I suppose the least kind review I could give of this game is that it is pickup and deliver with a bunch of random crap in between.  Because I tend to feel the mechanisms of a game more than the theme, I am left wanting...wanting to go play Merchants Of Venus.  

However, as a fan of the show, I can say this is a nice implementation of the Firefly license.  The components are great, and the game design is passable.  The biggest draw to this game is that it lets you revel in the 'Verse.  

That being said, even if you can swallow the mechanistic underpinnings of the game, there's an awful lot of luck here for such a long game.  I think they key point of tension is trying to take the minimal amount of crew and equipment along on your missions to maximize profits, but if you slice that too thin you will be frustrated by the die rolling. On the other hand, if everyone just gears up all the way, the encounters rapidly get too easy.

On the whole, I don't think many would have given this game a second look if it weren't for the Firefly name on the box!

RATING: N/A
Everyone who loves the show will love this game and should stop reading.
It is space smuggling game like Merchant of Venus but placed in Firefly universe. You pick your leader and your Firefly type ship and start recruiting new crew members, buying equipment and making business contracts with less shady and shady characters (like Mr. Niska). You can do legal job which pay miserably or illegal if not immoral jobs that pay quite well but you must be careful not to be caught by alliance patrol. Whatever you do you must also avoid contact with evil Reavers when you are outside of the Alliance sector. There are multiple scenarios and all the time players are immersed into the space western theme.
The only drawbacks is big turn downtime and complete lack of player interaction. The only conflict between players is when deciding who will take captain Mal and the rest of the original crew. This, they say, will be solved by the expansion.

[b]Update:[/b] Huge, bloated, tedious setup and unbearable downtime made me change my mind about acquiring this game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[3 plays] For the sake of sloth, I'm pasting something I already wrote when asked to compare Firefly to Merchant of Venus: 

Both these points of comparison [that both are pickup-and-deliver games with a space exploration theme] are somewhat true and somewhat not true. The theme of MoV is definitely space commerce (with a side of exploration). The theme of Firefly, though, is Firefly. MoV is straightforward commerce--buy low, sell high, and make profitable investments. In Firefly you're more like a crook pulling capers, though some jobs may be legit. And Firefly is very much a game whose mechanics were developed to fit an existing theme, not vice versa. 

Likewise, MoV is definitely classic pickup-and-deliver, while Firefly is only sort of P&D. Some of the "jobs" you and your crew can accept in Firefly involve taking stuff from A to B, but others just involve going to one place and doing something. And the things you have to do for the endgame goals (though they vary) don't tend to be P&D. Also, skill checks are a big element, which is totally absent from MoV. 

The pacing of the games seems significantly different--though I'm definitely speaking from semi-ignorance. At this point I have played MoV 50 times and Firefly 3 times. In MoV, you're looking to get off the starting block fast, start making money right away, and make every turn count. If you get too distracted by rambling around looking for exciting space relics, you might have fun adventures, but you're not so likely to win the game. And although there is some degree of equipping your ship in MoV, that's not nearly as big a deal. In Firefly, you need crew and equipment to be successful. 

I think there's a tension between spending time to build up a better crew which will make you more successful at the goals, vs. progressing more quickly toward the goals but with a lesser crew and lesser chance of success. In the few games I've played, I definitely have tended to get too good a crew and be beaten by people who moved faster, which is probably partly because of getting drawn into/distracted by the theme, and partly my tendency to be conservative and wait to strike until the odds are in my favor. 

It may well be that MoV seems tighter and faster to me because I've played and analyzed that game a lot more; if we play a bunch more Firefly, a similar dynamic may emerge there. That actually seems likely, because the game is similarly race-y. In the early learning phase we might be just wandering around in our spaceships going "Hey, isn't this cool!", but when we know the game better it's likely to become painfully clear what the average game length is, what the value of a turn is, what things are worth taking the time to invest in, and so forth, and Firefly will seem less like a rambling, picaresque space adventure, and start to feel as tightly strung as MoV does now.

RATING: 8
One of my favorite games.  Firefly is much more than it looks at first glance.  There is a sandbox element to it that a lot of people overlook.  You do not need to be a fan of the show to enjoy the game (although it will help you get the references and jokes hidden throughout). Overall it is a glorified pickup and deliver game with a lot of other options on the side.

RATING: 6
There are some nice thematic elements that evoke elements of the show such as misbehaving and how frightening the Reavers are but overall it's a design out of the 1980s with all the randomness. There are dice rolls and card pulls galore here as if it were inspired by Talisman and published in 1988. And just like Talisman, it's not that there aren't better decisions than others, it's just that luck can overcome your good decisions and reward someone else's longshots. One bad turn can wipe out several turns worth of work and set you back an hour.

You take a group of people and 1 or 2 will get wiped out by bad luck, 1 will do extremely well and make it look easy, and the rest will be in between. So you go along for the ride to see which one the dice and card gods have allocated you to be this day.

RATING: 6
This was a lot of fun to play.  Although it took 3 hours for 3 players to get through the intro scenario.

I had watched and read a few reviews which caused me to go in with some hesitation.  The luck and downtime were stressed, but other than one situation, none of that appeared for us.

Everyone kind of planned their turn out while the previous players were going so there wasn't a lot of waiting around, especially when someones second action was to buy and you could start your turn.

As for luck, we only had one situation when someone ran afoul of the Cruiser and rolled 3 1's which caused 3 of their employees to be caught.  Other than that, one the first couple of Misbehavin cards got turned over it became clear to everyone that you really needed a decent enough skill level to have some confidence that you would pass.

Overall, a pleasant game.  Not quite as thematic as say, Merchants and Marauders, which adds a lot of flavor text, but still great.

I would definitely play again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Licensed products can be pretty dreadful, re-skinning a very ordinary game mechanic with some pretty pictures from a TV show. But this game is put together from scratch, and obviously by people who love Firefly. The game mechanics conjure the events of the show and it feels pretty much like a RPG, where every player is a rival captain recruiting a crew, finding work, doing the job and getting paid. There is so much randomness and player-choice available that no two games should ever be alike.

The materials are created with care and attention, and are based not just on the TV show, but also some of the visual "extended 'verse" of fan created and licensed product. The dice (two, even though only one is required) have a little Firefly image for a six. There are four actual firefly models as player counters, and a Reaver Trans-U and a lovely Alliance Cruiser (this last is a bit wobbly on its stand).

If you are Browncoat, this is must buy.

There seem to be some problems with distribution and not many stores in the UK can get hold of it. So it's great that AmazonUK has copies for sale (10 left at time of writing).

RATING: N/A
A very good game that could have been great. This game works well with my family. They love the shopping aspect. They love that the game isn't about combat. In some respects, the game is similar to Merchant & Marauders. But in my opinion, Firefly is superior. You get to put together your crew, whereas in M&M your crew doesn't really have a face. Plus the missions are more interesting here. However, I'm not a big fan of the Misbehave deck. You should be able to plan for a job and put together a crew and supplies that meet the needs of a job, but you do that only in a general sense here. Success at the job comes down to the Misbehave card that you draw--at that is largely luck of the draw. You prepare for success at Misbehaving in the same way regardless of the job. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Early impressions very positive.  The game is a little like Merchant of Venus if you only left in the satisfy demands part of that game and spiced it up a little with  other chrome, so I'm going to make that comparison repeatedly.  

At first, I thought Firefly had fired MoV.  After a number of plays, I don't think that's true.  Firefly is not even as close to as good a competitive economic game as Merchants of Venus.  It's just that it tells a better story.  The choice between both games is really about whether you lean toward narrative in your pick up and deliver or a leaner, more cutthroat economic game.  If I'm honest, MoV is probably the better designed game.  The decision to keep all cards that have been drawn face up for anyone to examine is fucking GRIM.  If you want to play at all efficiently you have to get down to the business of at least vaguely knowing what it is in those discards, which is brutal for game pace.  Bad design there.

You don't need to be a Firefly fan to enjoy the game, though it does help.  Also, dear god, don't play with more than 3 players, downtime city.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a space adventure game that scratches the itch perfectly. It helps greatly to be a fan of Firefly. This game seems like a true labor of love for the Firefly franchise. If you aren't a fan, is this still a fun game? I think so, but with some caveats. The setting of Firefly is the Wild West in Space. If you want a variety of aliens and ship combat, look elsewhere. This is a game about basically trying to make a living and avoiding the law and Reavers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
If you love the Firefly series and like games with LOTS of random events and don't care if you will have 1 1/2 minutes of down time (i.e. time where you do absolutely nothing in the game) per turn per other player in the game (i.e. in a four player game you will do nothing for approximately 4.5 minutes before it is your turn again) then FF might be a game for you.

For me the game absolutely BLEW CHUNKS.  I liked the few episodes of the series I watched so I thought I would give it a try.  The sheer randomness of all aspects of the game from drawing cards for jobs you could do, to drawning cards to see which goods/crew you might be able to by (in the firefly universe they have no websites or ebay to know what is available anywhere so you pick from random stuff when you need to shop for upgrades or crew)to every space on the board you may have no encounter or may get stopped and lose your goods after moving one "space".  When you arrive at your destination you may have to "cause trouble" but of course the trouble you have to cause is totally unknown to you until you draw a card to tell you the terms of your trouble. If you FAIL you not only don't complete your job but you lose the job and may lose 1 or all your crew in addition (crew which may have taken you multiple turns to assemble and with an average of 5 minutes downtime per turn in a 4 player game means that your last 30+ minutes of work can be vaporized with one bad draw/roll combination).  Once you are behind with a bad FAIL you will likely never even come close to catching up.

I would rather be punched in the arm than play this random pile of puss again.

RATING: 7
When i saw the word Firefly, followed by "the game", the jaw dropped, the wallet opened, and amazon was sending a copy my way.

Having loved the series, and Serenity the movie i could not wait to play this one..

To sum it up:

Thematically: yes, its firefly, the characters, the random, the art, the minitures, the reavers... Absolutely superb. Fan boys/girls will love the art, images and stories.


Gameplay: scenarios without house rules and modifications are way too long, no pvp, and the mechanic is very very samey. As a game it lacks real decisions and the tense moments. The excessive random element becomes very annoying.

Overall a must for firefly fans, but hardcore gamers without a brown coat will walk away disapointed.

RATING: 4
The theme is implemented very well and is quite immersive, regardless of the "Serenity" crew being scattered around. You buy crew and equipment, get jobs from contacts and try to fulfill them. All fine and I really like the idea of story cards, which give you various goals to achieve, instead of the all-too-common "player with most money wins".

Unfortunately, the game suffers from a terribly long playing time and huge randomness - never a good combination. I don't mind a little randomness, but the problem here is that bad luck is often extremely punishing. A bad card draw or die roll may set you back several turns. When you fly, for example, you can as easily have no events or be stopped in the middle of the movement and lose your cargo, passengers or crew members.

The worst, however, is the "aim to misbehave" deck, which gives you completely random challenges without any way to predict what you will encounter. When you have to "misbehave", you basically flip cards and hope for the best. One card even requires you to have a specific character, which is simply bad design.

Another instance of bad design is that you can have three active jobs, but you cannot voluntarily discard them. If you lose whatever a job requires you to transport, you need extreme luck to replace it, and you are likely stuck with an unavailable job slot for the rest of the game. If you are unlucky, you may even have all three slots blocked and be out of the game.

Despite the problems, it was fun for a few plays (my enjoyment of the TV series surely helped), but I think I'm now done with the game.

RATING: 6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game is everything that I've wanted in an adventure board game, and more.  It's deliciously thematic, with a wonderful crew and equipment system.  Everything in this game is very personal and gritty.  You're not simply picking up a "job" from an anonymous person -- you're doing a job for a specific contact of yours, and if you complete it you will gain a specific advantage with them;  if you fail, you could stand to lose not only the money, but even your reputation with them and others.  Wonderfully flexible system that is elegant and deep without feeling complex.  

There is luck in this game, but it can always be mitigated by crew and equipment.  "Luck favors the prepared" as Edna says, and that is certainly true in this game.  At first glance, the event cards seem brutal in their luck, but the crew and equipment cards are so powerful that they more than counteract. A wise captain is able to shrewdly build a ship to mitigate the luck that comes his way. In my first playthrough of this game, my endgame ship was so powerful that it was like a well-built level 3 ship in Galaxy Trucker -- event cards kept coming my way, but I had a +9 bonus in combat, a +7 bonus in influence, and a +5 bonus in repair. I hardly had to roll for any encounters, because my ship and crew was so overpowered to be able to deal with that. Granted, it took a LONG time in order to build that ship and crew up, and I had to take a lot of risks and cut a lot of corners to make it to that stage, but finding a twisted path to navigate the complex 'verse of Firefly to get to that point is the fun of the game.  As a big Galaxy Trucker fan, I really felt like there is a shared spirit of luck dependency and luck mitigation in both games, and while you can build a nigh-indestructible ship in both games, there is the time pressure from your opponents that makes it infeasible to reach that optimized level of perfection. In Galaxy Trucker it's a real-time pressure as the sand timer ticks down, and in Firefly it's a turn-based time pressure as your opponents are trying to gear up to get strong enough to take on the end-goals sooner than you do.

There is a huge effect that crew and equipment have in mitigating the cascades of adverse luck that are due to come your way in Firefly: The Game. You'll all draw crappy cards -- what matters is how well you've prepared, and how creatively you recover.

In addition, I love how jobs in this game are divided along two axes -- morality and legality.  Jobs can be legal but still be immoral, and can be illegal but yet be moral, and the way that it all flows together so smoothly really communicates the gritty nature of the universe.  Fantastic space adventure game.  If you're looking for a game that is an excellent economic game of cargo and delivery and route-building, then play Merchant of Venus.  If you're looking for a game that immerses you into a universe full of adventure and despair, hope and greed, corruption and redemption, and lets you fly around in a battered ship and try to make your way in this place for a couple of hours, then play Firefly: The Game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
I was extremely impressed by the thematic integration in this game. It really has the feel of an adventure game, with random events occurring that seek to tell a story more than to offer a mechanical advantage. And yet the primary mechanisms revolve around pick-up-and-deliver. These two aspects blend together nicely to really give the same feel as the TV show on which the game is based.

Players will cruise their Firefly-class ships around the 'verse, avoiding Reavers and the Alliance while trying to complete jobs for (often less than reputable) contacts. Certain jobs will have more negative consequences if you run afoul of the law. You will also gain crew and weapons, most of whom are expendable, but some of whom are appropriately powerful and could cause real heartbreak when lost in battle (most of these you will instantly recognize from the show). 

Like most games based on a property, familiarity with the source material is a definite plus in terms of your likely enjoyment. It's not an absolute necessity, and it may even create some interest for players who don't know the show. Still, the narrative the game creates is far more compelling when you are already invested in the characters before the first card is dealt.

RATING: 6.75
Firefly makes a great attempt at capturing the thematic flavour of the Joss Whedon stories, in the 'Verse.

What it doesn't do is streamline the play; I find that it plays as slowly as AH, which means it had better offer a lot for the time gathered.

And for total die-hard Browncoats (this may be you folks), it does a fair job of that, but if you tire of the play trying to drag yourself back up for another attempt at misbehaving or a goal, only to fail, then I'd say steer clear, except for those occasions where do you want to be with total die-hard Browncoats.

There is a lot of card-drawing activity, every turn you Fly, and that takes up time.  There is a lot of die mod calculation every time you have to misbehave, unless you have the Ace to bypass the card.  And there can be a lot of back and forth trying to realistically get money to do things you need to do to win- and it may still be for naught on a bum die roll.

If anything, Firefly is a little too realistic- players who have ill-fortune with cards or dice may see themselves passed, through no particular strategic fault.

This is thematic gaming, folks, love it or leave it.

Starting this at a 6.75, though I'd like to make it higher for some terrific efforts at realism, I can't because it just plays a little too slow for me.

Too bad- this is a fine game in many ways.

RATING: 8
[b]tl;dr[/b] — Don't know from the show, but as a storytelling/adventure game this works great.

This is a "story game" first and foremost—it provides, via cards and mechanics, a series of dots that you and your friends can connect to spin an engaging yarn of your time out in the black.  In that regard it has far more in common with [thing=21523]Runebound[/thing] (and the like*) than [thing=131646]Merchant of Venus[/thing].  As it stands, this is a pretty middle of the road pick-up-and-deliver game—but it is an [i]awesome[/i] story game.

I suppose I should admit that I am not a [i]Firefly[/i] fan—I never got past the first couple episodes of the TV series (especially when they were pandering so obviously to segments of fandom that I am not a member of**), though I did enjoy [i]Serenity[/i].  This is important to know as my flaccid interest in the license in no way detracts from this fine game.

As a licensed product this one transcends—to an amazing degree—the usually poor treatment such things get.  The bits are all gorgeous and high-quality, especially the money (and I loves me some paper money***).  The game is mechanically sound, works, and provides an interesting storytelling engine.  Instead of phoning it in the designers and producers definitely heaped some love and skill on this.

Speaking prematurely and from the hip I get the impression that the sweet spot for this will be 3p—I fear that with 4 there will be just too much "story" flying around as well as too much downtime waiting to get back to yours.  But we shall see...

RATING: 8
Good, fun game.  Not exceedingly competative because there is not a lot of interaction between players in the core game.  All players have the same goal which is established or chosen at the beginning of the game but from there, each firefly captain is on their own to assemble/hire a crew, find jobs, and buy weapons and upgrades necessary to accomplish that goal.  I think this one will be liked by the wife who is not a fan of heavily competitive, back-stabby games.  PS,  all the artwork is great regarding money, cards, game board, etc.  The components are nice, but nothing to scream about.  Overall, the game does give an atmosphere of the show and the threat of encountering reavers and Alliance ships provide tension and a risk of losing everything!  It is fun to have the opportunity to hire a character from the show as part of your crew.  Obviously they are the best of their types (engineer, pilot, etc).  You do not need to be a fan of the show to enjoy this game but it helps set the atmosphere.

RATING: 3
Not familiar with the show, but I see there was much attention applied to grafting the license to the game.

I know this show, and subsequently this game, has its fans.

The components, art, and graphic design are great.

However, the game is too long for the game play it provides. 90 minutes would be ideal, 2+ hours? - it is too random and repetitive.

I'm fine with randomness for a narrative driven game (ha ha, look what happened to me), but the narrative doesn't come through with this game. 

My biggest complaint - I feel the movement mechanic kills it - too clunky, draw a card for each space? -  more importantly, a few bad movements (bad events) can wreck you early. This would be forgivable for a game that lasted 1 and 1/2 hours, but 3+ hours, no.

Still, I see the appeal of this game. However, if not for its theme, it would be a complete stinker. There are some neat mechanics - perhaps it could be fixed, but dang it, ugh.

RATING: 7
This is a fun game where I think that the theme has been properly represented in the mechanics. There are many wonderful things like if you choose to behave or not, or the point that you have to pay your crew every time you complete a mission, the different types of contracts... everything works very well. On the dark side, in my opinion, there is excessive luck involved in the game. Not only dice, but the type of cards that you draw at every location the probability of having a better or worse characters to include in your crew. For me, that is what really changes the game and creates the differences, not how do you play the game.
Taking that into account, the best way to approach this game is just to enjoy the mechanics, try to have a good time while traveling over the space and compete for the best possible result, but do not waste to much time planning great strategies because everything will depend on your crew.
Positive:
1. Very thematic
2. Fun to play
3. Good artwork
4. Several things to do
Negative:
1. Excessive luck involved
2. Maybe is a bit long for what it is
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.2
It was a little confusing on my first go around but in retrospect that may have simply been because I didn't fully understand the rules and the there a lot of cards on the table.  On my second try after a thorough reading of the rules and FAQ I see it's a pretty straightforward and fun game. As long as you prepare a bit before running headlong into new jobs, plus some good die rolls, you'll be fine.

On my second game I probably played it too cautiously because when I finally started to actually work the goals I did all three right in a row without any problems. Doh!  

I played while  rewatching episode 1 which makes the game so much more enjoyable (if not a bit longer).  It's fun to directly correlate the show to the game.

Aside from the theme the game is pure Ameritrash, which I'm fine with but there aren't many real decisions and you will rely heavily on good dice rolls and card draws, especially early in the game.  Picking jobs and deciding who to hire and what equipment to buy is important but I often found myself just buying the best item I could while trying to shore up my weaknesses where I could.

So I enjoyed the game a lot but I'm also a fan of the show.  I'm not sure how this will stand up with someone to whom the theme means nothing. If you're all about strategy and decisions then maybe this isn't the game for you.  For fans of the show though, this is a must buy game.

RATING: 7
I'll be in my bunk.

This game is way more fun than I expected for a game based on a TV show. It's really fun. Actually, I think it's the most fun non-party-game in my collection.

For the first 4 or 5 games, there's no way the first recommended scenario would take the suggested amount of time of 2 hours. Double it, perhaps. But now after 8 games it really does take about 2 hours, occasionally a bit less. We also use a few house rules to make things a little less annoying.

One problem: The rule book is organized well but suffers from grammatical errors that obfuscate the rules. For example, the writers use the phrase "the dice" to refer both to multiple dice and to a single die. One of the rules said to "roll the dice", so that's precisely what we did since the game provides two of them. But we later figured out that you are in fact supposed to *roll a die*. It's a minor gripe that doesn't detract from the fun of the game, but it did make the learning curve steeper than it should have been, and it is an error that should not be there.

Still, just playing this game is worth the time you put into it. Did I mention that it's fun?

Needs a big damn table.

[Edit: After a dozen plays I'm getting a little tired of it. Even at two hours it goes on about twice as long as I feel that it should. I'm occasionally unwilling to play it, but it's still very enjoyable.]

RATING: 4
I really, really want to like this, and I really don't.  It feels like this game is so close to being awesome, even if you don't consider the appeal of the theme. Plus, there ends up being huge luck elements with the cards, which don't seem to be particularly balanced.  Even all of that might not have turned me off of the game if it was a short game.  But the games I've played have been a solid four hours, and this with the recommended starting goals that are supposed to last two hours (one recommended by the rules and the other by the people in the Firefly forums here).  On top of all that, the rulebook is a disaster, with lots of holes and ambiguities.  Update: After my third play, I made the following comment about game length somewhere on the Geek:  The beginning and end can be fun, if only there wasn't so much middle.

[hr]
2014-10-27

When I was reading the rules, I thought the game would be great. Sadly it disappointed me because the downtime is excessive (the worst sin a game can commit).

I never watched the TV show, but I did saw the movie. Still I played the game with some friends who did see the show and it seems they enjoyed it a lot more than me due to this. 

At first everything was fine, the gameplay is very similar to Arkham Horror (move to a location, draw a card from that location, resolve situation with skill rolls, apply consequences/rewards, rinse and repeat) but after a few turns the game became boring for me thanks to the long downtime and the repetitive nature of the turns. I do like AH, perhaps because it is a CoOp game. 

A big part of the problem is the movement mechanic. On paper or seems fine, but drawing a card for each space is clunky and takes a lot of time. 

Player interaction is very low. Great art and components.

Firefly also has lots and lots of uncontrollable luck, practically guaranteeing a long game. The rule book had some holes in it but the FAQ answer them. 

Bottom line, it is a long game, with high downtime, high luck factor and low on decisions. It is gorgeous though but for now I'm selling my copy of the game along with the (unplayed) pirates expansion. I see only theme here, no game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.25
Is is perfect?  No.  Is is still Shiny?  Yes,... yes it is.

There is so much theme crammed into this little box that I'm genuinely surprised it hasn't exploded into a cloud of Firefly-themed rainbows and kittens.

Still, the two big negatives you may have heard about it are nevertheless true: 

1.  the game can certainly go on for too long, if you go by the rules as they are provided. I, however, aim to misbehave.  It is very easy to shorten the game length simply by marking how many of the victory conditions you'd like to play through on a given victory condition card, e.g., just set the goal for 2 of the 3 conditions, or even just one for a quick romp.  It's essentially modular in this way and suffers nor ill effects.  Thus, in my opinion, this is a small (and immediately correctable) gripe, unless you just HAVE TO play by the rules, in which case, I'm willing to bet my ship that this game was never for you anyways.  Yes, pulling a card from the appropriate deck for every move you make is slightly clunky and possibly tedious for some, but I like it better than, say, rolling a die, since it allows for more detail and modular upgrading from future expansions.  

2.  There isn't much in the way of player interaction-- especially in 2 or 3 player games.  Sure, you can mess with other players every now and then by having the right card show up at the right time, but that won't happen too often.  Also, you can actually snatch crew from another player when in the same space and under the right conditions (which likely won't occur all too often). Other than that, though, this just isn't that type of game.  It's more of a race, really, with some varying obstacles thrown into player's paths via dice rolls, vying for the same limited resources, and dealing with other player decisions throughout the course of the game.  
So, as long as you're expectations are in line with this type of a game, there's no problem.  If you were expecting BSG, or Twilight Imperium, then you'll be disappointed.

With all that said, is it fun?  

The short answer is: undoubtedly so.  

As a fan, I can't tell you how excited I was when I happened upon the chance to hire Zoë into my crew (while playing as Mal aboard Serenity).  What more can you ask for?  Those are the moments that make the game shine... and there are plenty to be had.  

Being boarded by Reavers sucks... like it should.  Having to stop for the Alliance to seize your stolen goods and fugitives sucks...as it should.  Flying around willy nilly in the verse while building up your crew, gear, doing odd jobs, and upgrading your ship is everything it should be... and it should be awesome, just like the TV show.  

At the end of the day, this game is made for people who enjoy Firefly and the Firefly universe... and with this intent in mind, Firefly the Game is a categorical success.  Go buy it.

RATING: 6
My first Gale Force Nine game and the only one so far I'm interested in. Firefly is a thematic pickup-and-delivery game. It's about "skilling up" your crew and ship in order to pass three types of tests to accomplish jobs and earn money. Unless players are skilled up, the random factor can be brutal. Expect that one or two players get hurt so bad that they just can trail the pack. Once up to speed though the challenges become a breeze. Until then, a whole game night will be spend.

I enjoyed my one game (with the pirate expansion) but for the duration there's not enough diversity to play repeatedly. As it is, I rather dig out my old copy of Merchant of Venus.

RATING: 8.1
 This game oozes theme. If you are a fan of the TV show you will undoubtedly enjoy all the references on the various cards. This can actually be a downside as all the reminiscing can delay the game. This will subside after a few plays and you've had a chance to see most of the cards.

 That all being said about the theme, this is a pickup and deliver game through and through. Get a Contract here, go over there and pickup goods, then go over to that other place to deliver said goods. Use the money to buy Gear and hire Crew to make your picking up and delivering easier.

 So pickup and deliver is the base mechanic, but it is not the end, only the means. The game is about the Story that is selected at the beginning of the game. This gives the players specific Goals that need to be accomplished, usually in order, to win the game. It may be as simple as get the most Cashy Money. Or it may be something a bit more involved than can be contained in this here comment.

 And I think it's this Story driven game play that, while being one of the best parts of the game, creates the biggest problem with the game play. In essence it's a race,  but you never really know how close anyone is to the end. Without this I think the game loses its sense of urgency. Fewer risks are taken and this has a tendency to prolong the game unreasonably. The excitement gets stretched out and by the end it starts to feel mundane, less aggressive even.

 Now is this a problem with the game, or with the people playing it? Well the people of course. But people invariably screw things up and it should the responsibility of the game to make people... better.

 In the end, Firefly: The Game is an amazing game that just has a tendency to last longer than it should. It needs less Pax and more misbehavin.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Highly enjoyable game with a lot of love poured into the components and the gameplay. Unfortunately, there are just a couple elements that knock the experience down a few pegs. Firstly, the card-drawing mechanic for basic movement is very clunky, and this can not only make each turn feel like a grind, but makes down-time unbearable for other players. In my personal games, this has been solved using a die roll for movement and a smaller (incident-laden) movement deck for any events that occur.

Finally, the overall objectives tend to feel a little anti-climactic; as soon as you've established a decent crew, you will navigate and annihilate everything with ease, without any real risks, so the game simply becomes a race. The expansion may help with this a lot.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
I'm a huuuuuuuge fan of the show... HUGE.  That being said, the game is a 6.5 on mechanics and I gave it a 1 boost for the theme.

Why 6.5 for the mechanics?  Well, it's kind of boring.  If you remove the nostalgia of being in the Firefly verse, it's just a pick up and deliver game.  There's no real challenge other than rolling dice and hoping you make a roll.  Here's the game in a nutshell without theme.

Pick through a random selection of Jobs.  These Jobs are pick up and deliver from one space on the board to the other.  Then you can either move one space for free (mozy) or you can pay a fuel for up to 5 spaces.  Every space you move like this you draw a card depending on the area you're in.  If you're in Alliance territory, you draw from the Alliance deck and if you're on the Edge, you draw from the Edge deck.  The decks are essentially the same.  There's mostly "nothing happens" cards, then some move a NPC ship around card, and a few "stop here and get some extra cash if you want cards".  They're usually a bore and a hassle to go through.

Then you get to your space a turn or two later.  You deliver stuff as long as you have the required icons to finish the job and you get money.

That's generally it.  You can buy crew and equipment which is mostly just having fun with the theme.  I played against 3 players and by ignoring all the cool theme stuff and concentrating on the actual mechanics, I had more jobs done in the end than anyone.  Clearly I had some aptitude... :)

Again the theme is great, hence the 1 point bump, but the game as far as mechanics goes is boring; not sloppy or ill-conceived, just not a challenge at all. I love Firefly, I love pick up and deliver space games, but honestly, I don't think I'll be buying this one.  I just don't think it'll get played enough.

RATING: N/A
In Firefly: The Game – based on the popular Firefly television series created by Joss Whedon – players captain their own Firefly-class transport ship, traveling the 'Verse with a handpicked crew of fighters, mechanics and other travelers. As a captain desperate for work, players are compelled to take on any job — so long as it pays. Double-dealing employers, heavy-handed Alliance patrols, and marauding Reavers are all in a day's work for a ship's captain at the edge of the 'Verse. Firefly: The Game is a high-end thematic tabletop boardgame from Gale Force Nine (GF9) and the first in a series of tabletop hobby board games and miniatures games from GF9 set in the Firefly Universe.

RATING: 7
It's a little bit of RoboRally meets Merchants of Venus but a lot of Firefly theme with a couple of intersting mechanisms thrown in.  I think this is comparable to pick-up/delivery and customize spaceship aspect from Merchants of Venus but different enough that I probably like this game more.  It has a set of sequenced missions to achieve (for victory), similar to RoboRally.

Basically, the first half of the game everyone is building up their crew and ship upgrades, making money by various objectives, and acquiring a full set of reputations, in order to pursue the game's selected goals.  The last third of the game is spent gaining the actual goals and they cascade fairly quickly, and must be done in sequence.

It probably plays optimal with 3 players and that keeps downtime to a minimum and the pace of the game clocks in at a reasonable amount of time, for the type of game that it is.  For me, it's enjoyable with 3, and probably a bit too lengthy with 4.  The Firefly theme suits the game very, very well.

RATING: 7
This is a very tough game to rate because it is a kind of interesting level up/pick up and deliver/press your luck kind of game on its own but it is just improved so much if you enjoy the license.  I am a Browncoat so I enjoy the immersive theme.  If I did not, I would probably play something else given the length and relative randomness of this game (it is not a completely random game by any means and experienced players will have a huge edge but the best plans can be undone by randomness and the game is best played for the experience in my opinion). This game does what I want it to do very well -- it creates a rich immersive game with a very limited amount of source material.  It is also a solid gamer's game but it would not be an exceptional one if not for the theme. The length is a bit of a problem with more than 2 or 3 players for me because the decisions are not sufficiently engaging for the amount of downtime. RATING: 4
Before, due to an unusually bizarre combo of cards, the game ended before we had a chance to really see what it did. Now I've played a full game of it, seen what's there, and don't care for it. It's in the trade pile.

Two players. It was okay for the first two-thirds, but then we hit some major snags towards the end:

1) The endgame is Talismanically irritating. Basically, I had to get through four Misbehaves and a skill roll to achieve the final goal and win the game. My opponent had to get through three Misbehaves to get the second goal, then move to where I was and do what I was trying to do. It was unlikely I wouldn't win, but to just give up seemed wrong. So we went through our respective motions. I failed twice, but so did he, so it was a prolonged battle for the places we knew we'd get.

2) Misbehave cards where you fail unless you have a specific character (River Tam). There are at least two of these. That is some bullshit game design and not only because River Tam was the most irritating part of the show. Also the Misbehave deck itself is so ridiculously random. This is exciting at first, but then it just gets tedious. Getting stopped on card #4 by something that can only be passed by one card in the game? About as fun as a kick to the head.

3) Jayne's Hat. This card bugged me for several reasons, most of them being how absurdly powerful it was. Having this won me the game, and all I had to do to earn it was find it in the deck first. Stupid.

4) The goals themselves. As with other games, it's a race, but the race is along a known course, so there's only one path to victory. Sure, there may be different ways to get to those checkpoints, but you still have to hit each one, in order, so you always know exactly where everyone is. 

5) When all was said and done we'd played for a little over two hours with two players. The Reaver ship did nothing the entire game and the Alliance ship did very little as well. With more players they'd probably do more but then you're talking about a longer game that still has other issues. If I'm playing for three hours anyway I'm going to go with Merchants and Marauders or Merchants of Venus and not this.

6) Jesus this thing is a table hog. Thirteen decks, plus their discards, plus the board, plus tokens, plus player boards. 

This game has two major competitors and I don't see where it offers anything over either. I've been told play time, but I find that hard to believe and also don't really care. I'd rather play a slightly longer but better game than a shorter and lousier one. Or just play a different game if that's all the time I have.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game is an easy 10. It scores high on the fun scale, regardless of whether you are a Firefly fan or not. But fans of the tv show 'Firefly' or the movie 'Serenity' get an extra bonus because the game is literally oozing the flavor and feel of the tv series. Its not often that a game both captures the look and feel of what its based on AND plays as well as this does. 

EDIT: After an additional number of plays, introducing a number of other players to the game, my review above stands. 

One additional note worth mentioning is that the base Firefly ships are really 'the best' ships for the game, because they are so well balanced to the game. The special ships that can added to the game through expansion purchases are generally more 'specialized' and not necessarily 'better'. For instance, the 'Jet Wash' comes with a few ship expansions that must be paid for, decreasing your starting credits. This can really have a detrimental affect on your first few turns, if you are not careful.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
2-5 Players
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
So it has taken me forever to figure out why I don't like this game. Firefly is a great show and yes, it was about picking stuff up in one place and delivering it to another place. Except that the show really wasn't about shipping at all. The show was about what happened between, during, and at destinations.

Further insight, Firefly (the ship itself) is a character in the show. Less so in this game.

---

This is not a "pick up and deliver" game. It is a race game. The first player to do [fill in the blank] wins the game.

The game seems to offer a variety of choices (1 of 8 possibilities for first action, 1 of 6 possibilities for second action). That said, certain actions are only available on certain spaces so the actual number of options is less. Thus "flying" is the main mechanic of the game. Unfortunately flying is repetitive (move, draw, move, draw...) and random (maybe movement ends, maybe not).

The game is too repetitive and too random for such a long game. To deal with the longness, the game tries to be strategic by having long term goals and added rules for searching discards. Unfortunately the strategic elements fail because the show was more tactical, as seen by the "fly by the seat of your pants" aspects of dealing with what the next bad thing to come your way.

Missed opportunities:
-- Some cargo tokens could have "?" on one side, so you don't know if you are actually carrying cargo or contra. (Same goes for passengers and fugitive tokens.)
-- Money was tight on the show. It is less so in the game.
-- The board is huge. It would be nice if there were spaces for the appropriate card decks next to the appropriate planets instead of the decks taking up even more space on the table.
-- The location of the Reavers Cutter is always known, so it can be avoided. Instead face down tokens could be used, where only one is actual ship, so the location is always unknown. 
-- Card organization seems backwards. The "instant" win condition is at the bottom of the mis-behaving card, but should be at the top so you don't read the rest of the card.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
With Blue Sun and Kalidasa

RATING: 7.5

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The rulebook is pretty terribly written. The writer seemed much more interested in explaining how each rule has a thematic tie-in with the TV show rather than how to actually play the game. This makes certain sections appear not where you would expect them too, terminology confusing, and some rules to be ambiguous. Also, the examples don't come with pictures so they are hard to follow along.

I actually wasn't a fan of the show of the 4 or so episodes I've watched (I know, travesty!), so keep that in mind if you read the following.

I like how there are different scenarios that can be played, which is pretty rare for a game that isn't 1 vs. all or co-op. Also it's nice that they tell you that the intro one is a bit shorter. Overall they all have you perform a bunch of jobs, just some require you to do a specific goal-related jobs, so in practice they aren't hugely different. I think I prefer the ones that you need to get a certain amount of money more, because that incentivizes actually selling off cargo and what-not (otherwise for the ones where you just have to do certain jobs once your crew/upgrades are good enough you don't really care if you lose money, have your cargo seized, etc).

For the most part this game is very heavily pick up and deliver, on the lighter end of the weight spectrum. Go to certain sectors to pick up jobs, go to the starting location of the job to pick up whatever you're transporting, and then go to where you need to drop it off. All in all, outside of the misbehaving cards (in which case you should buy a bunch of stuff to up your stats first) and needing to be a little bit more careful navigating if you're transporting illegal goods or have a warrant on you, despite allegedly having 4 different job types.

The market decks are significantly different from one another in terms of what icons they give you, but since a lot of the icons and traits serve the same function, just applied for different skill tests/able to start different jobs, I'm not sure how much what you can find will change your play style. The leader you choose in the beginning though seems like they would change up play style at least a little bit.

I wish for the navigation cards when you try to move around had greater differences between them, but I liked the risk aspect of it and it was thematic.

Completing jobs for different people gives you different benefits, but they don't seem groundbreakingly different from each other, making each region of the map feel relatively similar.

The only interaction in this game is if you are in the same place as someone else you can trade/steal their disgruntled workers, and movement of the reaver/alliance ship. While a single instance of this can be game changing, it is still possible to have games where there is no interaction with the other players at all, besides possibly taking a more risky job because they are further ahead of you, and I think that is probably one of the bigger flaws of the game.

Some people might not like the art is just screenshots from the TV show, but not a big deal for me. The money is paper money but the artwork on them is gorgeous.

Expect to need a large play area for this game.

If you're a big fan of Firefly, I think this game is a must have. They definitely have tons of little quirks that make thematic sense (e.g. if you get in a fist fight your weapons no longer help you in the skill test, your crew demands payment which you can choose not to give, but then they become disgruntled and might choose to join other ships). If you're not into Firefly as I am, the game runs too long for what it is, but with fast enough players it is still moderately enjoyable as a thematic pick up and deliver game.
