RATING: 8.5
I'm adjusting this one up after a few more plays.  

This fits a magical space where my noncompetitive friends enjoy playing it for the theme and the fun of the journey, and my competitive friends can play in the same game trying to block each other and slit their throats without ruining the game for the more casual people.  That's a really hard thing to get right, and my group isn't so especially fond of Firefly that they're giving the game more credit than it deserves.

This also feels like the spiritual successor to Starfarers of Catan to me, the only Catan game I ever liked (because it is nothing like Catan...), and one of my favorite games from when I was first introduced to "real" games.

RATING: 6
A fun game with a great theme. The cards are all very thematic and fit in with how things happened in the show. For example, I had River Tam in my crew and she allowed me to roll a dice before every skill check and she may or may not add bonuses to the check. It perfectly fits with how River was in the TV show-- always doing her own random things but, in certain circumstances, be amazingly awesome and save the day.

Overall, I enjoyed playing this game however I don't think I need to have this in my collection as the play time is too long and I don't think it would hit the table very often. It really is an experience. You have to be committed to sitting down and playing for a few hours and getting involved in the world and theme.

RATING: 6
Type: 1-4 player space exploration and questing game, largely multi-player solitaire

Best with: 1-2
Weight: Medium
Duration: 3-5 long hours
Notes: 

Players take on the role of a Firefly-class space ship looking to complete quests, earn money, smuggle goods, raise a little bit of trouble planet-side, and reach game-winning goals before the others, all while avoiding both the law and the reavers.

There are some downsides. First, this game has an absolutely huge footprint on the table. The components are gorgeous, but the board is huge, the player cards are huge, there are many piles of draw decks around the board, and so on. This game requires a serious table to play, even solo.

Second, the game is also very long. It's not a really deep game, but it can get very long depending on which winning goal is used. This can make the game very boring.

Third, the game has almost zero means of interacting with other players. Beyond moving the reaver ship around, there is nothing one player can do to another. This is simply about racing around the universe and doing quests faster than the other player. There is very little chance involved as well, so it's not like you can hope for bad or awesome dice rolls to wipe out a lead.

Still, the flavor and artwork is just gorgeous, and if players are ok with the solitaire-like play, have a huge table, and don't mind the length, this game does look like it can be fun for Firefly fans.

Similar games in my collection: Race for the Galaxy (largely multiplayer solitaire, space theme), Mage Knight,

RATING: 5
Rating after a single, five-player game. We played the easiest introductory scenario.

Frankly, this was pretty dreadful. The game's rules are typical ameritrash chaos, with lots of stuff you have to remember at any given moment, and the rulebook isn't very well organised at all. No index in this sort of game, really?

But the thing that killed it for us was that the game took twice as long as it should've, and the biggest issue is the downtime. Maybe it's less severe with four or three players, but with how little player interaction this game offers, maybe playing it solo is the best solution.

It's the sort of game that can be easily expanded, but its core gameplay needs serious tweaking to be even remotely enjoyable. The randomness of the Misbehave and movement cards is terrible.

Some good ideas in an overproduced, underdesigned title. A great shame, given how good the source material is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Excellent theme, fun to play. If you are a fan of the short-lived Firefly/Serenity series, you'll like this game. You are the owner/operator of a Firefly-class transport. You take on missions, fly around the 'Verse, wheel and deal, and try to make money. They did a great job of recreating the look and feel of the Firefly universe. You can play solo missions and avoid Reavers/Alliance ships, or play 2 to 5 players. There are also several expansions that add ships and missions.

I only have a couple of caveats. Although most of the cards, board, cash and other items are high quality and look great, I think the miniatures used for the various spaceships are a waxy-feeling plastic that seems chintzy and cheap. I do note that there are some very nice paintable resin miniatures available - for a premium price...

The other issue is the manual that comes with it. I don't think it's very good. The rules actually aren't that complicated, and I found watching a few reviews on Youtube really helped to explain how to play.

I've read a few complaints that the randomly drawn Reaver action cards are a little too powerful. You can be doing well in the game, then get attacked by Reavers and lose half your crew and get set back tremendously. To me, that's actually true to the TV series, so it's not a flaw for me.

Overall, very enjoyable!

They successfully captured the theme of the game through components and art to gameplay mechanics. 
The game is largely fetch and deliver quests, but it matches the theme of the show and does successfully make it feel like you are a ship captain trying to keep your ship and crew flying. 

Bad: 
Even with the expansion, there isn't all that much player interaction. 
Turns can be excruciatingly long if you have anyone that is AP prone. 
Lots of components to set up and put away.

RATING: 8
We're long time Firefly fans and this game didn't disappoint. The goals to succeed are pretty tough, but that's the challenge. One variant we had to include in our house rules was the "magnetic rule" - because neither one of us really wanted to battle it out with the Alliance cruiser or run into the reaver ship. (We didn't want to hurt one another either - not quite to that cut-throat kind of stage yet) Anyway - the magnetic rule was one that moves these pieces one space towards the closest opponent after each move/play. That way - they almost become "hunters" rather than waiting for someone to run into them .... Makes the game a bit more challenging - but the goals already do enough on that front. Great concept and love all the pulls from the various characters and storylines from the show and the movie.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
I really wanted to love this game, but it's an overlong snooze-fest, completely lacking in tension or difficult choices. The turns are so long that it forces you to either start overlapping turns (e.g., "You go ahead while I figure out what I'm going to buy"), or everyone sits and watches and waits, and waits some more, for their turn to come around. Overlapping turns sounds like a good solution until you've got 3 or 4 players simultaneously doing some portion of their turn, and nobody has any idea what the other players are up to, much less who's winning.

Worse yet, even your own turn is fairly boring. It's a very lackluster pick up and deliver game with no tension. Just make sure you buy enough gear and crew to have a decent shot at completing a job, then flip a few cards and see if you succeeded. Then do that a dozen more times until someone (finally, mercifully, can I go home now?) announces they've won.

This game is the essence of multiplayer solitaire. I've heard that some of the expansions fix this somewhat (most notably, the pirates expansion), but too little too late for me.

Traded.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Firefly: The Game is yet another successful adaption of a TV show from GF9! It captures all the feel of the sadly short lived show- find a crew, find a job, keep flying!

The rules are a terror to explain and you should be prepared for this when getting set up for the first time (it takes me over 40 minutes to cover all the important nooks and crannies), and yet the game plays fairly smoothly when you actually get started!

Players manoeuvre their ships around the 'verse, making deals with big-dog contacts, shipping crew, cargo and contraband from place to place, and shopping for ship upgrades, crew and equipment. Its a space merchants game that works, and it works well at that. Mixed in with this merchant premise is a classic [i]Talisman[/i] style 'move your dude, draw a card, crap happens to you' adventure mechanic.

There's lots to do with plenty of important decisions to make. The game also has a spade full of luck too though, and sometimes it feels like the 'Verse just points right at you and says 'no'. When you are winning you feel mighty indeed, but when you are losing it feels like you are helplessly spiralling out of control with no way of return.

Due to this game's excessive length (usually 3+ hours) any major setback will not only cost you the last hour or two of effort but also put you out of the winner's race, making your whole game a demoralising losing battle. Uncomfortably I've had two players just quit the game outright in the few games I've played so far!

Different objectives and even a solo option give plenty of additional ways to mix up the overall feel of the game and causes players to recheck their strategy from time to time.

The expansions have so far also covered players looking for more direct confrontation with a Pirating & Bounty Hunting variants, as well as adding more complexity with different ships and plenty of extra places and items. Note though that as expansions are added in the game becomes increasingly over complex and fiddly.

Non-fans will probably get less from the experience, but if you are a fan of the show and maybe even just a fan of Sci-Fi Ameritrash this one could be well worth a visit!

Pimped mine up by hand painting the ships and swapping out the active player marker for an actual Stegosaurus toy.

Rating dropped from 9 to 7 over time as there always seems to be someone sat having a bad time and being miserable for 3 hours in every game! Misbehavin' without the proper preparation is the main mistake I've seen, which only leads to increasingly worse positions. Its usually 75% their fault due to bad decisions/rushing in too early and getting in a rut, but Firefly is one of those games that likes to punish players who continue to make bad decisions after their initial mistake.

The problem is I have encountered several gamers who after doing something reckless and messing up will then continue to make the situation worse by blindly trying again even though it didn't work the first time, making the situation worse for themselves over and over. Sometimes bad luck will then add on top of this making them even more frustrated and reckless, creating a vicious circle of self defeat, killing their chances and their mood. This bad atmosphere can sap a lot of the enjoyment and sense of accomplishment from the more successful players.

The most important tip for Firefly players:
Preparation, preparation, preparation. Better to have a slow and steady early game and then catch up at the end when you have everything you need to complete jobs first time around then risk blowing your whole game on Misbehave cards too early.

Progressive Rating: 9-8-7

Captain's Victories:
Corbain x2 (RPoBx1, Dx1)
Marco x2 (RPoBx1, Dx1)
Monty x2 (RPoBx2)
Nandi x1 (Dx1)

Ship Victories:

Artful Dodger x2
Walden x1
Inteceptor x1
Esmeralda x0

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
A superb game hampered by fatal flaws. Gorgeous components, great theme, some really fun mechanics. I'm a big fan of the show and film, and was really looking forward to playing this game...until I played it. It started out wonderfully - was easy to learn, and we were off to the races quickly. However, the issues make it a game I will not return to.

First, it is too long. Way, way, WAY too long. We played a scenario that was listed as being two hours. It took five. Five hours. With four very experienced players, who were not taking breaks or fiddling with their iPhones in between. If I'm going to play a game of that length, it has to have much more depth - Twilight Imperium, Eclipse, or Civilization come to mind.

Second, it is way too repetitive. Turning the navigation cards over again and again and again as you navigate through space becomes painfully boring. We hit the worst possible cards in the navigation decks repeatedly throughout the game, taking away their impact when they happened.

Third, it is way too punishing. Losing a single "Aim to Misbehave" challenge fairly early in the game can set you back hours as you lose your crew, causing you to spend a frustrating game trying to catch up to those who rolled the dice well.

Other people love this game - I will never play it again. I thought it was great at first, but once the true grind of playing it for so many hours set in, I was done. There is just not enough there to justify my time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 3
My rating of 2 is based on the selection criteria of I won't play it again ever in any circumstances and this is one of the very few games I can say that about.  

This does not mean it is a bad game.  Just not a game for me.  It simply did not click with me.  After playing 3 times I did not enjoy any of the games - not even the first which I won.  I felt it overstayed it's welcome by several hours.  I found the learning curve incredibly steep considering the limited choices.  It seemed to me detailed knowledge of the cards in each card stack for each planet was essential to make informed strategic choices.  Worse it punished those who fell behind. For me it felt slow, tedious multiplayer solitaire,  In all 3 games it seemed those in the bottom knew they were going to lose after the first couple of hours but had to pretend to have a great time for 4 or 5 hours while waiting for those who'd got ahead to finally win.

[Edit]
Upgraded to 3 after watching the TV show with my husband.

I still would never play it again:

4) For me it outstay its welcome after about 2 hours

RATING: 6
The graphic design is great, inspired by the series and consistent with it. The components are very good, even the insert.

It is a indeed a luck based pick-up and deliver game. There are no deep choices to be made besides pushing your luck or not at certain occasions. The tactic and strategic levels are very low, you depend mostly on the luck of the draw and the dice rolls.

What the game excels on is its theme. It manages to capture the atmosphere and he background of the Firefly series and Serenity movie in an impeccable way.

I would say it's a much lighter version of [thing=25292]Merchants and Marauders[/thing], with almost no interaction. I cannot say it's an excellent game, but I just love the genre and the theme.

Disclaimer: I have only played the introductory short adventure. Maybe the game experience changes with a longer serious mission.

RATING: 8
[b]Firefly[/b]

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8 -> 8)[/COLOR]

[i]Somehow a year went by and I wasn't able to play Firefly again. This was mostly due to not being able to plan another session with my friend who got me the game. I'm hopeful that'll we'll get to play again soon, which may involve learning the rules myself and setting up a 2p game with my son and seeing how things go*. I'd still recommend this game if you're a fan of Firefly; outside of that I need to play some more to see how it compares to Merchant of Venus [i](which is my favorite space themed pick up and deliver game)[/i].[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]This was a housewarming gift from a buddy of mine and on top of that he came over and taught us the game. Up front I'll mention that I am a huge Firefly fan, probably the best TV series I ever watched, so the first thing I need to mention is that this game delivers when it comes to taking advantage of the IP. I was lucky enough to get four members of the Serenity crew on my ship which was awesome. Everything in the game comes directly from different episodes of the show so you are fully immersed in the Firefly universe they whole time you're playing. 

Firefly felt a lot like Merchant of Venus if you added a healthy dose of screw your neighbor. I was able to sic the Reavers on the other players and poor Mike got smacked around twice by them. There is also some randomness in the game since you are continually rolling for skill checks and potential attacks, however you can hire crew with the skills needed to help offset the luck of the die roll. The different scenarios you can play change up the end game conditions for each game and can really change how you'll play the game. 

Overall I was surprised by how much I enjoyed my play of Firefly and I can't wait to play again. We are already setting up another play session, hopefully with four players this time. If you love Firefly you have to check this game out and if you enjoy pick up and deliver games with some take that thrown in I'd give it a shot too. I also need to mention that with teaching our game took two hours, but the time flew by and we couldn't believe how much time passed once we finished the game.[/i]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
It should probably be a 6 because there's so much stupid luck in the game, but the theme is nice and I'm sure that with more play you'll set up your crew and equipment so as to avoid most of the crap that the cards throw your way. You start with pick up and deliver quests that need to be fulfilled to earn money. Spend money to buy crew and equipment to amp yourself up. Then start tackling the hairy stuff that earns you big money, random hairy stuff like if you don't roll a 3 or more, you lose all your crew, or hey, if you roll 2+ you win the game (sure enough, I rolled a 1 and someone else won the next turn ... head shaking). If you can't tolerate that level of luck, don't play. Because if you over-invest to get rid of all the luck, you'll find someone else has taken some risks and won before you. On the upside, there's huge thematic goodness about who and what you can find at each location in the 'verse, with each major location represented by a deck you rifle through and purchase from. There's different scenarios so you can better match to the type of games you like. I'll play again, but geez I wish I'd had a better idea of the risk/reward offsets before that first game that went too long and was too frustrating because we kept attempting stuff when not as prep'd up as we should have been. Live and learn. But anyway that's a feel for the major decisions in the game ... how to plan your pick up and deliver stuff, when and what and how much to invest, when do you take risks. There's lot of rules wibbles about which side of the law you're currently on, whether moral or not, whether there's a warrant out on you not, whether you're an outlaw or not (carrying contraband or fugitives), all of which can have repercussions. Thematic goodness, but a few wibbles too far probably. If you're a fan you'll forgive it. If not, might be best to steer clear.

RATING: 7
"Pickup and deliver, in space, with some shenanigans. Probably best if you enjoy going after each other, and/or with a bit of roleplay. My first 2p game only took 55 minutes, which was a pleasant surprise."

What I like:
- I generally enjoy pickup-and-deliver, and this is a pretty good implementation of that
- Space theme is nice, and there is lots of flavor
- Multiple scenarios
- Quite a bit going on, but not too much
- Solo scenario (but I don't know if it's any good)

What I don't like:
- I would prefer a bit less direct interaction (e.g. reavers)
- I can see where it could run quite long

I went into my learning game expecting a 3-hour marathon. But in a tight 55 minutes, I completed my 3rd goal to win the game. It's an efficiency race, so you don't want to get caught up in buying too much cool stuff, or taking on creative contracts. Unless of course you enjoy the game because of the cool stuff and illegal contracts, which I suspect is why my experienced opponent lost. 

My initial 7 rating is for the introductory scenario. I think the "respectable" scenario would probably also be a 7 but might be lower because it may take too long. Most of the rest of the scenarios are of no interest to me because I wouldn't want to be forced to misbehave. 

I would put the weight around 2.7, just a bit below BGG voters.

RATING: 6.5
6 Plays - This game is about building a strong card tableau, while managing jobs and travel risks. The very limited player interaction really is a real negative, as is the use of the alliance and reaver ships which could have been implemented in a way that had a lot more significance throughout the game. Mostly, players simply move them about meaninglessly, resulting in them feeling superfluously annoying (mechanically). Players rarely need to give thought to either avoiding them or moving them. Occasionally though, the alliance and reavers will suddenly 'appear' and can be very brutal to a single player. The issue being that both their target and timing of appearance are both random, sometimes simply cancelling your chance to win and repeatedly beating the same player to tears. 

If you don't like Firefly the show, then you probably will enjoy this less - all the cards etc. make reference to something in the show which help the game make thematic sense. We always have Firefly playing softly in the background while playing this game. Plays fairly well solo & 2 player, plays great with 3. 4 is good, but down time is an issue. 

The cards are negative for a few reasons. 1. There's just so damn many of them! 5 decks of jobs + 5 decks of items + the misbehaving deck + 2 travel decks + discard piles for each = 26 decks... did I count them all even? Also, we found the job cards quite busy and people often missed cash bonuses they were eligible/ penalties or eligibility requirements (which is in turn affected by crew changes). Not sure if there was a solution here for a more 'intuitive' job reward system (though this is more a nitpick).

Often my partner and I play co-operatively i.e. we both select a solo mission each, and slightly adapt the rules as needed. Home brewed scenarios are relatively easy to formulate (like really easy), as are adaptations that can lengthen, shorten or change game play to suit players.


Finally, your card tableau is built quite slowly at first, but later, even the hardest challenges become almost 'too easy' to overcome with your well-rounded crew. The tableau is really fun to build, as you capitalise on every opportunity that the 'verse throws you, but is rather anti-climatic! 

Final thoughts? This is a game with problems from both a component AND mechanic perspective. So, so many decks of cards that contain so much information! The tableau is fun to build, yet the biggest challenges are at the beginning when you're still rallying a crew, rather than at the end when you're polishing your weapons. The largely dormant alliance and reaver volcanoes are a missed opportunity that occasionally erupt with game-melting, luck-spraying lava. Yet, it feels like Firefly and it is REALLY fun to travel inside this unique world. The integration of luck DOES add some brilliant tension that makes for great stories and moments. This is definitely the kind of game you'll recount with your friends afterward, though you will probably inevitably note its flaws as well.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
This game feels a lot like playing the "standard rules" in FFG's Merchant of Venus.  It's generally a pick-up-and-deliver game, but you can be waylaid (often for multiple turns) by bad card draws, resulting in turns where you accomplish nothing.  The theme is a plus here, as you definitely feel like you're navigating the Firefly universe.  However, the "named characters" from the show feel somewhat overpowered, if you're lucky enough to draw one.  I like both Firefly and the pick-up-and-deliver experience, so I can overlook some of the flaws of this game.  However, the "classic" Merchant of Venus is a much better game in this genre.

(1 play)

RATING: N/A
Hire you a crew, git ya some shootin' irons, maybe some fancy duds, and declare it time for some thrillin' he-roics.  If you're a fan of this cult classic cancelled long before its time, you'll love the flavor of this game.  If not, you'll find this a pale comparison to better-designed commerce-based games like Merchant of Venus.  The inclusion of brilliantly designed paper play money is a thoughtful touch that sets this game apart, IMO, from those which settle for mere cardboard-token money.  :)

The exansions are a bit frustrating (I've played them at a friend's house) as they chose to add new boards to either end, creating a super-long board that is difficult to fit on a table and hard to gather a group around.  Aside from that, though, the expansions add a ton of fun and new cards and mechanics, including the opportunity to go pirate and prey on other players, which changes the game from a mere race for riches to a very cutthroat space brawl.

RATING: 10
disclaimer: I can recognize almost every element of this game and the episodes they come from.

Playing this game is a lot like roleplaying. I think it would be fun for people who haven't watched the show (but way more fun if you do watch the show). Each game has different goals and stories- which is really fun! A two player game takes 1.5-2 hours. A three player game takes two hours. It's not very interactive (2 player), unless you do a lot of pirating and trading (happens more with 3+ players). It's pretty hard to sneak up and do pirating in a two player game (I usually just do two player). You can win by playing it pretty straight, but you can also engage in human trafficking (which is unsettling at the very least - but usually not profitable so whew).

It seems like it would be difficult to teach, but it actually doesn't require too much explanation to get started, and you learn best as you go along. I usually explain the game as people go pretty effectively, advising on how different elements work as they come up. My dad usually gets pretty flustered with some of my board games, and he navigated this one pretty effectively. He didn't do any amoral jobs and maybe only a couple illegal ones.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
August 2013: One game, four players, 3.5h. I've watched several episodes of Firefly and enjoyed them, but I'm not a fan of the show; the theme of the game is not that important to me.

The game reminded me a lot of [gameid=131646]: it's a pick-up-and-deliver game with a lot of upgrades you could apply to your spaceship. It's less strategic, has more luck, and a little bit less player interaction (there isn't much player interaction to begin with). However, the integration of theme is impressive. So I'm rating it a 6, the same as Merchant of Venus.

[b]General course of play[/b]: On your turn, you can perform two actions. The available actions are: move your ship, purchase upgrade cards, obtain contracts or "job" cards, and pick up or deliver goods. You can't do the same action twice. Winning conditions vary. The game comes with six scenarios, including one solitaire one. Some of them involve getting a certain amount of money, others involve successfully doing a number of skill checks at certain locations.

[b]Some more detail[/b]:

[b]Pick-up-and-deliver[/b]: The route planning is much simpler than MoV. No pre-printed routes. You are moving in an irregular grid. There are two regions of the board, an "alliance" region, and those outside that region (forgot the actual names, and I'm not a particularly a fan of the show). The big difference between the region is that the neutral alliance ship can attack you in the alliance region, the reiver ship outside the region. 

There are five spaces/planets from which you can pick up upgrades and five others from which you can pick up contracts, or jobs. Some upgrade and job spaces share the same space. These spaces vary by what kind of upgrades and jobs they have to offer. This is a bit less than the 12+ planets that MoV offers.

[b]Strategy[/b]: There is no supply-and-demand mechanic like in MoV. Instead, there is a deck of upgrade/job cards associated with each upgrade/job space. If a player is at an upgrade/job space, he or she goes through the *entire* discard deck and selects up to three cards. Then he or she takes more cards from the face down deck until he or she as a total of three upgrade/job cards. Then the player can buy (or select for job cards) a maximum of two cards from those three. So if a lot of players are obtaining cards from one particular space frequently, the player last to arrive at that space has a smaller choice of known cards. So there's some player interaction as players try to be the first to a particular planet to buy a certain discarded card or to draw one. 

Many of the upgrade cards give a +1 or more modifier to three statuses: fight, repair, or negotiation (I forgot the actual terms). Many things you do in this game requires a skill check: delivering a good, picking up a good, or moving one space with your ship. The skill checks focus on one of these three statuses. However, apparently the best strategy is to maximize all three statuses so that you're able to pass all types of skill tests, because the nature of these skill tests is random. I'm not sure if it's a valid strategy to focus on less than three statuses, or to focus more on ship upgrades (those that for example make you go move faster or require less maintenance).

[b]Player interaction[/b]: It's pick-up-and-deliver, and those games generally have low player interaction. As mentioned before, there's subtle player interaction for upgrade/job cards that players can obtain at particular planets. When players are sharing a space, they can trade resource with each other. Players sharing a space can also steal crew members from each other under certain conditions. (Crew members are like upgrade cards.)

Another source of player interaction is the race aspect of the game. Players compete to accomplish the same goals. You can either fully equip your ship before attempting these goals, or try attempting them with the risk of losing crew members or other detrimental effects. I think this is one reason why I lost my game of Firefly; I didn't consider accepting the riskier jobs (which pay out much more) until later in the game.

[b]Fiddliness[/b]: Less fiddly than MoV; there are way more counters in MoV than in Firefly, and MoV's supply-and-demand mechanism adds more fiddliness. However, upgrades and jobs are all represented with cards. Considering you can have four ship upgrades, six crew cards, and three active jobs (without any other upgrades that increase these limits), this game takes up *a lot* of space.

[b]Summary[/b]: In Firefly, the luck factor is considerable, interaction is a bit too subtle (no negotiation and minimal situations where you can directly attack an opponent) and the game drags a bit (our first game, four players, took 3.5h). However, the integration of theme is excellent, so fans of the show, especially non-gamer fans, should enjoy this game. It's a game I wouldn't request to play again, but I would love to introduce it to (patient) non-gamers who love the Firefly series. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Pick up and deliver game with excellent integration of the TV show theme. Crew members, bosses, jobs, equipment. It's all there. And it works. Plan routes, manage risks, deal with setbacks.

RATING: 7.5
If you never have seen the tv series, I am not sure if this is the game for you. 50% of the fun is playing with the old characters which I loved so much (and still do) from the tv series.

But objectively speaking, if you have never seen the series (and you should) it is still a great game. Some of the artwork, especially the supply cards are not that great. This is a huge contrast with the 150 credit bills that look amazing. The game mechanics are ok-ish. There is not a lot of interaction between the players and if you play it several times it can get a bit boring. Basically you would do missions to get money and you need money to buy a crew and nice gear. With a good crew and gear you’ll try to accomplish the story card. There is a lot of luck involved with getting a good crew and gear and drawing the better missions. It would be nice if the game integrated a way to play more tactical. 

There are six story cards, and for every game you pick a story card. A story card is a different way to win the game. In my opinion, six cards was not enough. They should have doubled the amount of cards.

The game uses cleverly the characters from the tv series and there are some great references to the show I love so much. For that it’s worth every penny. I hope they will release some (big box) expansions that will solve all the game mechanic flaws. The game is not as solid and as shiny as I would like it to be, but I will forgive all that, because it’s a Firefly game!!!

RATING: 6.1
After 5 plays and with the blue sun expansion, here it is. If you are a firefly fan, looking to travel the verse, dodging reavers and staying one step ahead of the alliance all wrapped up into a long evening's entertainment then this ticks all the boxes.  
If you are after a generic pick up and delivery game, there could be better out there. Having not played them though, I couldn't yet recommend. However, Xia, Merchants & Marauders, Merchants of Venus may be worth a look.

A few years on and i've finally played the above mentioned games.  Each have distinct features which i really like;
- merchants & marauders - the goods change each time from a port.  Really disliked the different captain ability, which try to shoehorn you into specific roles.
- merchants of venus - the route planning & low, medium & high market pricing are nice touches.  Can be hosed by a bad dice roll.
- xia - will have to revisit this one.

Overall, firefly is for role players who want to be immersed in the verse. Other pick up and delivery games have better streamlined mechanisms but lack character. So it becomes a matter of personal preference.

RATING: 9
Perfect variable very long game with fast rounds.
A must have for Firefly fan.
One of the best games I ever played.

[b]Pros:[/b]
- Tactics and skill are way more important than luck.
- Massive variability (different ship upgrades, crew, gear, jobs, events).
- Fast action paced playing. If you are not on the move, you are thinking about next round so you don't have time be bored.
- Jokes: Perfectly connected with Firefly series. Every card, person, ship, name and even the principle of the game itself. Everything will be familiar (and funny) to you if you've watched the series (but game mechanics are also very entertaining for those who haven't).

[b]Cons:[/b]
- Very, very, very long games (about 5-6 hours for 4 players).
- Even after a lot of rules learning, there will be still questions about specific situations. This can be frustrating (this [url=http://www.fireflythegame.com/howtoplay/FAQ.aspx]official FAQ[/url] certainly helps).

[b]Cons (1st play):[/b]
- Before your first game you must learn 18 pages of rules. Then you can teach your friends all of that rules in about an hour. If they are willing to learn, then all of you will be rewarded by excellent game mechanics and fun.

RATING: 7
Although it tends to be a bit on the long side, Firefly is one of the better games of roaming around space and doing odd jobs for shady characters. It basically comes down to picking up cargo of one sort or another and taking it somewhere, but this is done well enough that it doesn't become a chore. If you're a fan of the series you'll also get a bit of a buzz from risking taking work from Niska or scorning Badger's job offers. 

When I first played it I was told that the Blue Sun expansion is borderline essential, and I agree with that assessment. Aside from enlarging the (already huge) board, it makes Reavers much more dangerous than in the base game and thereby adds some welcome tension to proceedings.

RATING: 4
Slightly confusing rulebook at first reading, fairly straightforward gameplay, but sometimes hard to get an overview. Even though the actual board isn't very large, you'll need a very big table for all card piles, player boards and other paraphernalia. Most entertaining for fans of the show. Somewhat similar to Merchants and Marauders in the general gameplay feel. You'll definitely want to avoid playing this with people who suffer from analysis paralysis or those who can't plan ahead. Games can drag on for quite a while if you run out of luck and get caught by the Alliance, get parts of the crew killed off, or suffer other mishaps. You seem to have to build your strength for quite a while before attempting to complete story goals. Card names and quotes are rather good, and taken with misbehaviors actually make up entertaining, abstracted little adventures in all their brevity. All in all a better game than I thought it would be, despite being disappointed at first by the limited element of player interaction.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
As many others have mentioned, the theme is beautifully incorporated into this game. The art is great, the copy is great, and  every single game component is some sort nod to the Firefly franchise. The one game I've played was fun for everyone involved, including non-gamers who were on board because they enjoy the franchise. My overall opinion is a great way to game with people who might not otherwise play board games, but that it lacks the depth that one might associate with such an apparently complex game. I had fun, but as a moderately avid gamer, there's lots to quibble about, and it wouldn't ever be a top pick for me.

First, there's a bunch of fiddly mechanics that can be hard to keep track of, mostly involving conditional bonuses - I found Firefly more challenging to keep track of than some of my most convoluted games of Flux. Some of the conditional modifiers are fairly easy to track, such as missions that require a character who is a "pilot" or "mechanic", but others were not. As an example, I ended up with three different upgrades that impacted the outcome of a "salvage operation" card, on three different types of upgrades (ship upgrade, crew, and equipment), marked with inconsistent font/color combinations. Since salvage operations are uncommon, when one did come up for me I forgot about two of my modifiers until much later. Another tricky case was a character who had a modifier for a "crime" job, which is somehow different than an "illegal" job and marked in a different place on the job cards. You can end up with some fairly convoluted effect chains. It got to the point where I wished I had a computer tracking all of this because I was constantly needing to review all my cards whenever a new card was flipped.

The time estimates for scenarios seem quite low. I imagine that a group of experienced players who are aggressive (i.e., banking on lucky dice rolls instead of on slowly building up a crew) might be able to play short games, but most groups will be in for at least three hours. Our game lasted five, and it felt fun for the first couple and then began to really drag by the end.

Experience will matter. There's a natural game progression that won't be immediately obvious to new players who aren't familiar with the contents of the contact and supply planet decks - some contacts tend to offer easier jobs than others and some planets offer cheaper upgrades. Knowing where to find things will definitely make a big difference for early success as well as game duration.

Reward and punishment are too random for my tastes. The "big damn heroes" supplemental cards can create a game-breaking income if someone luckily manages to acquire several of them. One player repeatedly failed a job because she kept unluckily drawing an "aim to misbehave" card that prevented advancement unless you happened to have River Tam in your crew. I lost a huge load of contraband necessary for a job due to a random card flip I had no way of avoiding. There's no way to deterministically get contraband, so I thought I was screwed until a couple turns later when the stars aligned to allow me to replace everything I'd lost.  Combine all of these with the length of the game and you'll probably end up with players who are frustrated with poor luck despite reasonable decisions.

I quite liked the trading mechanic in the game and actually felt like some of the loftier goals were getting in the way of my just bopping around the 'verse making money. In fact, I eventually lost because I got so distracted doing fun trading jobs instead of keeping my eye on the prize.

I was with a group of people who weren't aggressive towards each other, and as such it sometimes felt like we were all playing solo (well, we were "racing", but watching progress was a bit challenging). There was little reason to trade or interact with other players. There's nothing that forces players to move the Alliance and Reaver ships onto each other, so they were just left floating around safely until someone got unlucky with a card. It was easy to wander away from the table while other players completed their turns without it being a problem, which started to happen more and more frequently as the hours wore on. I found myself wishing that the game was either more cooperative or more competitive.

As a side note, I highly recommend the "Bastion" video game soundtrack as background for playing Firefly. It's nice techno-western music that goes great with the theme.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Solid - I like this. The components and integration of setting are up to the publisher's usual superlative standard, as is the price - I'm sure they could have asked twice as much and got it.

However, there are better games in the genre. Merchant of Venus is better as a game - flows much better and has real economic drive. Merchants and Marauders is tighter as an adventure game. But, if you love Firefly and you like adventure games, aren't too fussy about the rigour of the ruleset, then run don't walk, it's a gem.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I've read a lot of comments that this game is "like Merchant of Venus", and while I understand why people draw these lines, they don't seem terribly accurate. The basic framework is very reminiscent of MoV. You have a spaceship, you're flying from point A to point B for a number of moon rocks. But that's really where it ends. MoV is a very streamlined game, sure there are a few non-intuitive points to it, but it has much less overhead than Firefly.

Firefly is more of a mix of Talisman and Arkham Horror. From AH it takes the specific card deck per location system, from Talisman it takes the concept of building a crew and armory that continually pushes your stats higher, the game is typically a race to complete a number of goals, and the travel mechanism, while I feel very innovative, even feels like Talisman's blind card draw on the "Draw 1 card" spaces. Firefly features skill checks similar to found in both the above games.

So saying it's like MoV isn't very fair to the game's actual heritage, as there's much more Talisman and AH in it's blood and MoV makes up it's skeleton of being a space delivery game, with none of the important features that makes MoV what it is.

Now that that's out of the way, I find this game to be a lot of fun. This is a space adventure game, and while it draws a lot from Talisman, it's multitudes beyond Talisman in design. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Includes: [thing=145481]Artful Dodger Promo[/thing] and [thing=176331]Card Pack[/thing]
[hr][b]House Rules:[/b]
[u]Big Damn Heroes:[/u] Promos do not replace base game cards, but are set off to the side. If someone selects/purchases the regular card, roll a die. On a 4, 5, or firefly symbol, you get the Big Damn Heroes version.
[u]Semi-unpredictable Cruiser/Cutter movement:[/u] Instead of "player to the right" moves the ship, roll a die. On a 1-3 result, the ship moves toward you. On a 4-6, the cruiser/cutter moves toward the player to your left.

RATING: 5
The game is thematic in the way in which the verse is recreated (all the planets, all the characters.)It recreates the conceit or McGuffin of the Firefly TV show. That is you are in a ship, doing missions. Other players are in other ships doing missions.

Go here, do this, get that, then go here, do this, get that.  Oh here's a Wash card you add to your crew. It helps you go here, do this, and get that. Same for all the main characters.

It's in this way that this boardgame doesn't really capture the heart of the show. That is one crew with very different personalities, each having demons and mysteries haunting their lives, coming together, trying to figure out the meaning of family while the rest of the 'verse messes with them.

I like the firefly show way better than BSG, but the BSG boardgame captures the heart of the show so much better (betrayal, co-operation, pressure, survival, resources ). 

For about the same amount of time 2-3 hours for both games, I much rather be playing BSG. In BSG you are at least somewhat involved in each others turns, in firefly it's just one big wait for your turn, then you do 2 things towards your missions of go here, do this, and get that, then you wait again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.3
Components - .9/1 Box is nice. Rules are disorganized. Easy to get up and running but provide troublesome when finding the corner cases. In game currency is by far the best I've seen in a game. It's so good, the rulebook disorganization doesn't cost this a tenth of a point. The board is well organized and the dice are nice (have a custom firefly icon on one side). The cards are standard, and the art is great. The ships are nice, except the Alliance Cruiser. The cruiser just seems cheap and flimsy. It doesn't stay on the stand well, it's warped, and looks cheap. To the contrary the Reaver's Cutter looks just like the film and the firefly's easily remind me of Serenity. 

Fun - .6/1 I'm trying to be objective with this. When looking for a game, this can easily drag into a long session of a snore fest. People have to actively be looking at things not on their turn, plotting/planning their next move. There is minimal interaction between players in the game. If you're not looking for a game for the sake of competition, but rather and experience, see my theme/personal rating. I do love this game, but as a game, I've found more fun in plenty others.

Replayability - .7/1 There are a set of several missions that come with the game and they are unique enough. Given the large number of card decks involved in playing (5 job decks, 5 supply decks, 2 movement decks and the misbehaving deck), even the same scenarios will have unique enough outcomes because the same strategy won't necessarily be available.

Strategic - .6/1 You can have a strategy, but you are at the mercy of the cards for quite a lot. At some point you balance getting every possible type of item/crew member/keyword with not waiting too long to accumulate said pieces so someone isn't too far ahead. A string of terrible cards in a row will put you in a hole and this isn't a forgiving game. Generally when you fall behind, you won't come back in it. It is worth noting the game doesn't eliminate players, but it doesn't really have any type of catch-up mechanism. I do still think strategy does play a part because a lot of it does boil down to risk/reward of running a slim/efficient ship (generally don't have enough to get to the end game) versus building a fully decked out ship (generally takes too long to complete).

Theme - 1/1 I'll prefix this with I love the show, I like the movie. It may make me have a bias, but I don't believe any game I've played has captured its theme so well. When I play this game, I feel like I'm a captain of my own Firefly in the 'verse. I find myself feeling like I can be doing everything right then fate slams a Reaver ship in my path and now I'm just scrambling to keep my crew alive. When I play this game, I do it for the experience because nothing feels like being in charge of a little transport/smuggling operation. Every time you go into space you've got a million things to worry about yet cannot do anything but hope you've got the necessary pieces to keep flying. 


Personal Rating - 3.5/5 I enjoy the game, but I feel like I can admit it is functionality lacking as a board game. If you strip out the theme, I think it ends up being a luck driven mediocre game. I think the theme is what makes this an awesome experience. When I play, rarely care whether I win or lose, I have a freaking fantastic time being the captain of a spaceship! Let alone a spaceship in a universe that I simply fell in love with in the show. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a pickup and deliver game set in the Firefly universe.  It feels very much like Merchant of Venus but with a lot of fan service for fans of the show (of which I am among their number).

In this game there is a global set of goals and the first player to complete all the goals is the winner.  The core of the gameplay is collecting equipment and crew for your space ship so you can better complete missions for more rewards with which to complete those goals or get more and better equipment and crew.  Like I said, very similar to Merchant of Venus right down to the science fiction theme.  I probably prefer Merchant of Venus because I feel like there is more to it but this is still a very rich and fun pickup and deliver game and like I said, as a fan of the series I love all the references and fan service in this game.

Since it is a race to the completion of a certain number of specific goals (rather than an end game point comparison for example) one flaw I can see in the game is, due to the random nature of most of the gameplay, lucky draws and better starts can give some players an unfair advantage.  The game knows this though and provides ways to alleviate that randomness.  When drawing cards from any deck you get to pick from not only the entire discard pile but can also draw up to three right off the top of the deck and choose from those.  This gives players a lot of options to find the best missions for them to accomplish their goals and even out the advantages some.

Like most pickup and deliver games though the scale of this one is huge.  There are over a dozen different decks of cards in the game and the footprint, setup, and tear down time is large plus it comes with a play time of about 1-1.5 hours per player depending on the scenario.  Also, despite how good it may be since that's all I hear people talk about with this game, the paper money is still annoying to deal with and I would probably almost always rather replace it with poker chips or ANYTHING else.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
No doubt, thematically it is incredibly true to the show, this IS Firefly in a board game. And that is worth something, sadly, next to the enjoyment of design and the great, thematic ideas the game play itself falls short. Something exciting is missing here.
Pick-up-and-deliver, route planning, legal and illegal (and sometimes immoral) jobs, hiring crew and optimizing your ship - all of that should be fun but in the long, long run of the game boredom settles in. It can take very long to get to the next planet/ port, the cards and dice roll add too much randomness for me (though, that is sure not out of theme), while you wait for your next turn there is nothing to do since the game is really not that complex to make you plan and strategize while you wait, then there is really minimal player interaction. I usually enjoy solitary game play but here I was not invested and therefor bored. 
I was disappointed, and then shocked when I realized we were playing for 3 hours and no one was even close to tackling the first of the 3 group goals which you need to win the game. Even for a first game (where you do visit the rule book several times to clarify how things work) that is way, way too long for what this game delivers.
I think I am willing to give it another try but for now "Firefly - The Game" has been one of the bigger letdowns of late. 5 points that likely might fall lower...
Update: 5 points I raised a bit to 6. This will never be a favorite, it takes too long for my liking, there is waiting til your turn comes around again especially when people go through stack of cards to make a choice, but it can be enjoyable, I seem to really enjoy myself for the first 30 min, then it starts to drag.

Fifty pounds of theme in a five pound box. This is probably the best themed game I've ever encountered -- they did a wonderful job of capturing the feel of the show in a board game.

My only qualm for this game is that it's one of those games where the players are basically sitting together playing separate games of solitaire.  There is very little interaction, beyond being able to sic the Federation or Reavers on someone, or occasionally trading.  It appears the upcoming "Pirates and Bounty Hunters" expansion was designed to address this, as it specifically creates direct conflict between players.  Hopefully that will increase my rating to a 10.

Much larger UK box has more room for expansions. Same height as US edition, but half again as wide.

RATING: 7
Took some time to get in to because of the not so clear rulebook. In fact it's a good solid space adventure game. Starting with a lot of pickup & delivery, ending with more challenges. 

Reminded me of a crossover between Relic, Runebound and Fortune and Glory - in space.

As in Relic, you traverse the void, and though you have more options, it is usually quite clear what to do on a given turn. As with Runebound, your hero (in this case, your ship) 'levels up' as you get more gear and crew to take on heftier jobs. But it reminded me the most of Fortune and Glory, as you encounter adventures and have to make skill tests. The mechanic that sets this game apart from F&G is in my opinion the 'choice' you have on your adventure cards. There is always an option, sometimes both bad, sometimes both good but you have more control. Therefore, it feels less random and 'sure whatever' as F&G.

Liked the game, disliked the frequent flipping back to the rulebook and some rules aren't even properly described (is captain part of your crew? If you have to kill crew, is that random or can you pick and choose, is a transport equipment that needs to be attached to a crew (presumably yes) and if so, is the BFG equipment that needs to be attached to a transport or a crew member to operate? etc). 

The movement mechanic is a bit wonky, with flipping over encounter cards for every step, but you get used to it pretty fast. All in all, liked the game, will stay in my collection and will definitely play it again.

RATING: 9
Even though, that we prefer Euros over Ameritrash games this one was a surprising hit for us. We were not that immersed by the theme to begin with - we had some vague recollection of the plot of Serenity, but was not big fans of the "browncoat world". Notably, we love sci-fi, so the theme was still a draw for us. This is a typical lazy Sunday afternoon board game where you can travel the universe, do different jobs and go through adventures which come with them. The idea, that the journey is more important than the destination perfectly applies to this game. According to our experience until the 70-80% of the game nobody really pursues the goals of the current plot, instead they enjoy flying through space visiting different planets, recruiting crew, and purchasing gear to them. In our opinion the Pirates and Bounty Hunters expansion is a must have - it does not only provide extra ships and side-objectives to the game, but more PvP as well. That expansion elevated the game from something which we liked to one which we love. It plays really well with 2 players, but perhaps 3 and 4 are the sweet spot for the game. With more than that it can take even more time to play - we had a four hours session with 5 players the other day. This is our major con against the game - the time it takes to play sometimes keeps it away from the table.
P.s.: After playing the game several times we were encouraged to rewatch the series. Our admiration of the design was augmented by the experience - even the smallest roles from the show are cleverly integrated in the game.

RATING: 6
Not so shiny. The same tired roll/skill-check mechanics (with one d6, so no curve), with way too many special rules and cases (and traps for beginners) to learn easily--often explained only in the rulebook. Only three skills, but a very large number of special character traits, and gadgets, so eventually you have to run around the 'Verse collecting everything possible to be able to survive random encounters (Fox, not Josh), eroding your crew and equipment, so you have to run around again. Also, you have to learn, what and where are which cards?

Firefly movement is tedious. For usually five steps: step; draw; and maybe a quarter of the time, encounter. Nearly all encounters have two options--while nice so you don't have to be an expert in all skills (or have all equipment) it slows the game. But after a couple encounters--"Wait! Where was I going?" Since evading the  Reavers or the Alliance stops your movement, in a four player game, the chances of another player being able to drop them right back on top of you is pretty high. And most of the goals are on the opposite side of the gorram 'Verse (3-4 moves).

While my initial impression of the game was very good, the same old mechanics get old fast. The goals seem too hard for quick play: why four successive random encounters? The more or better crew you have, the less you make from each job. Estimate one hour per player, for experienced players; double for new players unless everyone has read the rules, FAQ, and cheat sheets. Some parts of cards are a bit low contrast.

RATING: 7

When you play 2+ hour games they better be AMAZING (rebellion) otherwise, I am sorry, I generally am quite critical, still given the choice between BSG and this I would take this any day.

RATING: 9
Overall this is a fun, very thematic game. If you have not watched Firefly or do not enjoy it, then you will not get the most from this game. On the other hand if you are a fan of the show then you should enjoy this.

At its heart this is a pickup and deliver game, but the combination of theme mixed with the mechanics just makes the game shine. If you know you are going through Alliance space then there is a reasonable chance of an inspection - that's really annoying if you happen to be doing something illegal. But if you are in Border Space and the Reavers come by ... Reavers man! It's terrifying.

The game is not very hard or complicated and a 10yo can play with a little bit of early assistance. The challenge will be the game length - this is a game for rainy afternoon when you want to burn a fun couple of hours.

However for short family fun you can easily house rule it. e.g.
 - When doing a scenario, just do 1 task instead of multiple tasks.
 - Start with a bit more money all around (or give the younger players a money advantage)
 - Don't give younger players warrants, or kill their crew.
 - Don't attack younger players
 - Tone down the effects Reavers have on younger players or give them "Reaver Cloaks".

RATING: 7.5
A fun, thematic pick-up-and-deliver / adventure game that's reminiscent of [i]Merchant of Venus[/i] and [i]Merchants & Marauders[/i].  I like games that weave a cohesive narrative and this one definitely does that.

My favourite aspect is the ever-present threat of encountering the Alliance and Reaver ships.  The Reavers especially can be devastating.  My first game, the Reavers raped, ate, and utilized the skin of 10 passengers and 2 of my crew JUST before I reached their destination.  A spectacular failure, that job.

I've read complaints that the game can run long but I have yet to experience that.

UPDATE: (Some of) the expansions have made a good game better.  Though this game is now as bloated as [i]Arkham Horror[/i], and that's quite the accomplishment.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
[thing=138161][/thing] is a game in which the main actions are: move (spending fuel or not), buy equipament, fuel or parts for the ship, hire crew, search for jobs and fulfilling them in order to gain gain money and became solid with the contractor - trade and/or sudden but inevitable betrayal of disgruntled crew is possible when sharing a space with another player's ship.

In the moviments is possible to move 1 space, without hiccups or move, with the initial engine, up to 5 spaces, by spending 1 fuel. But, when travelling this way, for every space, a Full Burn card (event) will be revealed - most of them will be for nothing happens, others to move the Alliance ship (in the main quadrant) or the Reavers (in the outer rim systems), and, sometimes, a proper bump in the space, when the players will have to make a choice (normally to stop to avoid a bad thing or to gain something; or to continue, but losing the chance of getting the something or at a risk (a test) or cost (spending fuel, parts, making the crew unhappy, etc).

The jobs taken can be legal, as to take cargo or passangers from one place to another; illegal, as smuggling goods or help fugitives to escape; or crime jobs, which are done on the spot (the others require going from A to B), but are unpredictable, requiring the capitain and crew to do some misbehavin', which is revealing cards from the Misbehavave deck, that represents the unforeseeability of this sort of job (sometimes is required to fight your way out, to talk your way out, run like hell, and so on). For the crime jobs is best to go well prepared, with equipaments and a good crew, otherwise failure will follow shortly. The jobs that doesn't require misbehaving can be done with, normally, very little.

The players can choose their ship (at first, all are equal, only the name is different) and the Captain (these are indeed different, with some important unique abilities). After this, the Fireflies will be going around the system back and forth, stopping in key spots to do some business (buying, selling or looking for jobs). This is the basic game.

[thing=138161][/thing] works around scenarios. In the first, to learn things, the requirements are: 1) Be solid with 2 persons; 2) Have $6000 in the pocket; 3) Go to Ezra planet (where Niska lives). Done, this is it. The winner will be the first to fulfill the three objectives. Other scenarios change the requirements heavily, as expected. 

Now, onto the two most important things:

[b]Theme:[/b] It is there. Really there. From the language to the personalities to the places. For those that like the series, the ovearll story of Firefly is there. But is a grandiose scope. Firefly, the series, revolve around jobs, sure, but mostly is about people, the crew (mainly) and also in the people they trade, cheat, fight, talk, help, etc. In [thing=138161][/thing] is all about the jobs. They have thematic names, but in the end, people focus on take X on A and take it to B. I haven't see someone actually mentioning what the job really was, only what the needs of it were. This is a little of a bummer, however, I can't see a way to make the game as is more thematic than it already is. But I would be totally down for a [thing=34119][/thing] set in the 'Verse.

[b]Luck:[/b] This is the part of the game that can make even hardcore fans of the series turn their noses at it. Because there are a fine lot of luck in [thing=138161][/thing]. First, the events drawn are completely random: one player can cross a system without a problem, while you, needing to advance 2 spots, get hit bad twice; and this is also true for the Misbehave deck. Mind you that, in both situations, players can and must prepare as well as possible to deal with the occurrences thrown at them by the game. Still, you can be pretty well in the firepower and mechanical departments, only to be required a roll of the social skill of your crew. And, of course, say you did have a level for social tests, a 4, and is trying to beat the required number of 7, you will fail with 1 or 2; while someone else, with 1 in social skill, can roll a 6 and pass. There is simply no way of knowing what the Misbehave deck will ask of you - for the travelling events, at least most of them revolves around fuel and ship parts. The counterpoint is that the players know ahead of time that the Misbehave deck is a wild thing, and to keep and accept a job that requires misbehavin' is a player choice. Also, when buying equipaments, hiring crew and accepting contracts, there are open cards, which the player can look at, and is also possible to take facedown cards - so the player can know beforehand some of the available cards, and can also, if not is of interest, to push the luck on the blind draw.

A side note: the graphic design of [thing=138161][/thing] is, well, uneven for me. I don't like cards that have stills of series or movies - I prefer drawn art. So, the game could be a total miss, if wasn't for the [b]amazing[/b] art on the back of the cards and on the paper money card. 

[thing=138161][/thing] proved itself, to me, as the sort of game in the area of "play for fun". Yes, you can (not mandatory, but highly recommended) fun in any game, but there are those you play to challenge yourself, your mind, your dexterity, your wuick wits, your decision making under pressure, whatever. And there are those you should play just for the fun. To burn fuel on space, to dodge the Alliance while carrying loads of illegal goods, and drop them in the hands of a solid partner of yours. A game to load explosives and buy pretty dresses; to be bold and have flair for danger.

In other words: to aim to misbehave.

RATING: 7
not bad, but it did not wow me; however this was my first game of it, so I will reserve further judgement after more plays; so far, it reminds of an Ameritrash version of Merchants of Venus (which I feel plays more Euroish) - and as such, it has wilder swings of fortune in a way that I find a lot of Ameritrash games tend to have; the Reavers in the game are brutal; also you can try some really wild pushes of luck to get ahead in this game at times from certain illegal missions; in this game I mainly found myself constantly deciding whether to rush to my mission destination and risk running into bad luck, or slowly get to my mission destination and risk wasting time and falling behind the other players in points (money)

edit 2015-04-20: After more plays, especially solo and two player modes, this game has grown on me and the theme.  I enjoy playing it more often as a result.  Raised my rating from a 6 to a 7.

RATING: 7
Really pleased with this game. This is a really solid game system which creates an enjoyable narrative adventure. Gameplay is reminiscent of Talisman's move, flip a card, roll a dice rhythm of play but with much more freedom.

Component quality is good although I prefer artwork to cast photos which can make it look a bit cheap. The artwork which is included on the supply decks etc is great and very atmospheric. Rulebook was ok, could have been clearer and this carries into the gameplay which can feel a bit loose at times.

The game is hugely thematic, really captures the feel of the show's space-pirates-come-wagon-train adventuring. Nevertheless, I think the game would stand up perfectly well without the license. Fans will not be disappointed.

RATING: 4
Gameplay is mostly funneled through bland skill checks that are the standard "roll a die with some modifiers and see if you pass" variety.  It's also long -- plan for about 45 minutes per player, with very little interaction.  There's a high amount of variability in what you can buy, what quests you can take, how far you can travel, and what kind of cargo you can carry.  This isn't inherently a bad thing, but there are very few ways to mitigate bad draws, and that IS a bad thing.  

Didn't get what you wanted from the store?  Spend another turn.  Didn't pass the quest?  Spend another turn.  Couldn't fly far enough?  Spend another turn.  You know what's not fun?  Race games in which you frequently lose turns.  Pray you don't lose several in a row, or you will get intimately familiar with frustration.  

Lots of card draws and call-outs to familiar names, objects, and places is probably enough to satisfy fans of the show, but for players like me without that connection, it's quite dry.   The whole package has a staid game-plays-you feeling, as you continually draw a card and see what happens.  Throw in a rich-get-richer effect, and you have a real clunky game.  If you're looking for a better space merchant game, grab a copy of [gameid=131646].  If you're looking for a game based on a sci-fi show, go for [gameid=37111].

Probably the game's best trait is that it is so non-interactive that it is quite easy to drop out at any time, allowing you to go home and do something important like clip your toenails.

►ÉDITION : n/d
Éditeur, nb joueurs : 1 à 4 joueurs.
Éditeur, durée : 2h00 à 4h00/partie.
Éditeur, âge : 13 ans et plus.

►PUBLIC(S) QUE JE RECOMMANDE:
☺ Jeu thématique (ex : coop ou semi-coop, améritrash, univers adapté).
® À réserver aux amateurs du genre (série télévisée).

►JOUEURS, NOMBRE(S) QUE JE RECOMMANDE:
# Nombres non-déterminés.

►COMMENTAIRE(S) ABRÉGÉ(S):
+ THÈME : assez présent; relativement bien intégré.
+ Aide de jeu : 1 inclus. Bien détaillé.
- Durée du jeu : certaines parties peuvent s’éterniser.
+ Expériences multiples : plusieurs niveaux de difficulté.
+ Icônes : sont faciles à comprendre ou à mémoriser.

►REMARQUE(S) PERSONNELLE(S):
® Je recommande son essai car il pourrait être apprécié par d’autres joueurs (à noter qu’au moment d’écrire ces lignes, il s’agit du meilleur jeu "inspiré d'une série tv" auquel j’ai joué).

Premièrement, je n’ai pas regardé la série et je ne peux pas dire si le jeu en recrée l'atmosphère. Par contre, ayant déjà eu de mauvaises expériences avec d'autres jeux adaptés de séries télévisées, j'appréhendais donc celui-ci mais j’ai plutôt été agréablement surprise par l’ambiance rendue. De plus, lors de la mise-en-place, j'avais été intimidée par l’abondance de matériel alors que tout est expliqué sur les plateaux/cartes et organisé efficacement. Cependant, malgré que nous n’étions que 3 joueurs, que nous avions choisis un objectif facile et que personne n’a subi d’attaques, notre partie a tout de même duré 3 heures ce qui est trop long pour que j’accepte d’y rejouer.

RATING: 7
I waited a long time for this one and overall I'm not disappointed. It's a pick-up and deliver game, with a heavy dose of push of your luck...which is right at home in a setting that is themed more or less around smuggling and tight time tables. It runs a little bit long, but I think once players are comfortable running simultaneous turns (which the rule book encourages you to do) the length will drop considerably. Like GF9's other game Spartacus, all of the game's mechanisms are extremely simple but work together very well to bring the theme to life.

The most concise way to describe it is Merchant of Venus light, although there are a few differences. Firefly is more character driven and the misbehavin' encounter deck gives a better story arc to the game, allowing it to touch on the adventure game genre a little bit. Adding this little slice of Arkham Horror to the mix makes all the difference to me. It lets the characters and other game play elements take on more unique personalities, rather than the generic faceless pilot you get in MoV.

I am going to be careful not to overplay it though. There are only 25 cards or so in each market deck, (which to be fair is still quite a lot of cards considering just how many decks there are), so knowing exactly what you are going to see each game might get repetitive. In a Euro strategy game, predictability is good, in a thematic romp not so much. I don't think this is going to be a problem for long, since there are 8 or 9 game expansions coming down the line.

My honest opinion is that based strictly on its gameplay  I rate this about a 6, slightly better than I feel about Merchant of Venus. They did a really nice job of hitting all the beats of the show and sprinkling in plenty of offbeat references for the Browncoats, so my enjoyment of the game is a bit higher than that.

RATING: 7.5
I firmly believe this game will hold little appeal to people not familiar with Firefly... however I have yet to play with any non-fans, so we'll see!

First of all this game gets a special mention right off the bat for being incredibly eye-catching. Every little component and card is a work of art. It's nice just to have it sitting on the shelf.

That being said, this game takes up an INSANE amount of space! And time! This is primarily what puts this game into a 7 rating territory for me, rather than an 8. You have to be willing to commit some serious time to this one.

They really nail the theme - once gears get turning, you really get the feeling of "just getting by" and being all alone out in the 'verse. Almost every card in the game is sure to bring a smirk to your face if you're a fan of the show.

RATING: 6.5
Most games played with all listed expansions:
[GAMEID=145481] and [GAMEID=149433] from purchase
[GAMEID=149796] - 12-01-2014
[GAMEID=147736] - 18-01-2014
Also including [GAMEID=151953], [GAMEID=159651] and [GAMEID=179014]

I'm a Firefly (and Serenity) fan, and so thematically i like this game; it's full of the places and events from the series. I also like the mechanics involved, so this is a good game in my opinion.

What I think it needs is a little more variation in the missions (but hey, that's what expansions are for) and a faster start-up; the first few turns are dedicated to getting your crew together. I'm putting serious thought into creating some "starter crew" cards that let everyone start on the same level. 

The Big Damn Heroes expansion can also unbalance the game if you let one player get hold of more than one or two of them, as they add money that wouldn't otherwise be there. I'm working on a drafting system to basically give each player one of them at the beginning of the game, which may prevent the imbalance unless they're stolen away while disgruntled.

With those additions, I might raise my rating...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.09
It is a surprisingly interesting game. Not only it paints theme all over its rules and components, but it can also really appeal to a broad variety of players. There is rivalry to hire crew or buy items known to all players at the same time, one needs to manage his choice of jobs depending on his available resources, one needs to manage a budget to make sure that he keeps flying, working and paying his crew. That is strategy on a large scale, where a smart combination of all those aspects helps to win the game.
The objectives of each game is defined by the story chosen at the start and the first player meeting them wins. How to do it is up to the players but they are always reachable. A player may be slowed but cannot be eliminated. Twists and fate may well tip the scales the other way.

RATING: 10
I played a complete game of this at SPIEL 2014, and fell in love. This is pure thematic gold. I'm a huge fan of Gale Force Nine's line of licensed board games. The more I play this game, the more I appreciate it.

The game has incredible replay value with a grand total of eight Setup Cards, and 21 Story Cards. Some, like The Blitz Setup Card allow for much quicker play, while The Browncoat Way helps balance the many various ships, and make selecting a ship or a captain first a real hard choice. Combining these, and other, Setup Cards with the many Story Cards make for one hell of a customizable game. You can play complete matches in anything from one hour to many hours of epic play with a full table of six players, and a longer scenario.
